O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, embracing its applications and terminating with its demonstrations and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my notice that I should accompany this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is rare in our region and is strange to all, if it is omitted from the science and left out, only the small descriptions of the ancients remain in books that the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the emptiness, and the closures of the understandings and the displacement of the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or I seem to recall that I may restore life together with the arrangement of this physician according to the mode of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I shall bring together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and the other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as is proper
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is proper that he who interferes should learn in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he grasps the judgment of members, and the forms and the joints and the separations of these, and knows the bones and nerves and limbs and the number of bones, and the movement of veins and the resting of them.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates teaches us that one must not fear the unknown, for with work comes reward; and the same in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We must say at the outset of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things to be learned is often led astray by fear and scorns the homes; just as I have often seen more of these things which are interwoven with this science than those which depart from it and from sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish man who, when he has opened an abscess or the head of a woman, has so bled that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus there is another case which treats a stone of a bladder of a pig, and the stone was great; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in the hon [bladder] for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I have already been called to treat this case, and I saw the condition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and indeed if it were to be pulled out, it would surely kill him.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus there is another case which treats a duke from our land who had a broken limb, and with the bandage it caused a wound; and the physicians of this place constrain the fracture above the wound as these stars are by strong ligament, and do not allow any blood to come out, and leave it thus until the limb is whole; and they command that it not be moved; and when the limb is whole and the piece is gone, it is lost forever.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am ordered to come to him, and I hasten to come to loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, it is without pain and without feeling any discomfort.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption is already confirmed or the limb is unsound, and I cannot heal it; and it continues to displace until the limb is entirely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another sign which makes the swelling worse is that it bites and stings, and then becomes inflamed by the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound that is infected with melancholic humours, I do not know that it can be cured except by touching it with fire so long as anything corrupted can be removed from it.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, know well, that the work of the hands has become divided into thirteen parts: that is to say, there is peril in many things; and I shall show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, you must be wary, for if the fools speak badly of you, they will do you no good.</start_of_turn>
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take up your weapons carelessly, and undertake your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way if by the grace of God you come to health and peace; and leave the contagious diseases of grief far behind; and stay away from those things which make you doubt, and take comfort in what you can.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	Foreigners depart in boats of their warnings: “Do not take my advice badly for a disease, for you are called foolish like me.”
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and medicine, and the chapter orders from the head down; and forms of instruments, and instruments of cautery, and everything necessary for the work
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with amputation and incision, and abscesses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; and the chapter orders and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and fractures, and similar matters; and it orders the lord chief justice to bring the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we recalled from the work, it is proper to say the quality of the aid and the gentleness of complexion
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid and the gentleness are the longest words and the most subtle science and the greatest secret; and about this there are many sayings, and they agree on this; and I am silent about their words, because I fear their length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for any complexion or matter, because there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion hot in matter, and a complexion dry in matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, mixed with matter, some say that cautery is a great aid; others say that cautery is of no avail for disease except when it comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For indeed the nature of fire is hot, and should not be a cure for fiery diseases by heat, nor from dryness; thus those who say the opposite that cautery does great aid to fiery and dry diseases that arise from the humors of the body
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, no fire has come between me and fury except that which has experienced it, and which knows by long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of the complexion of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the issues and the space of their pains; for other temperaments we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them are settled and agree with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, child, that cautery with fire is more effective for secret healing than burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only from the member that is being cauterized, and does no harm to any other member except its name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another, causing grief and bringing diseases to the member; and by chance often causes harm to the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not make this worse, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have learned through experience and the length of my service and study in this art, and it is based on truth; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to hide the secret which is returned or fire, and the quality of this work, as it demonstrates the healing of diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know this, son, that it is necessary to apply the cautery at the proper tension and without haste.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, for the harmful effects that result from it are driven away by the action of the cautery; and even though the cautery is for necessary pains that are violent and urgent, which cannot await the tension of a greater harm to the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, dear son, if like madmen they make; for the disease which is cured by cautery has no return; and he says thus; but it is not so easy, for cautery is but a medicine which moves the complexion, and dries up the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for its haste of value, and for the excellence of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And indeed, it is known that the disease does not come once according to the complexion of the patient and the cause of the disease and its virtue; and are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of food and other things, if these cauteries are administered in place or if there is little excess of superfluity and moisture, as with dense cautery for pain, and other things, and part of the pain does not return again; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that cautery is not called medicine, and it is seen; but they do not believe that cautery is worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cautery that is behind medicine because whenever we administer remedies for any disease and they do not work, we then administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore although cautery is at the back of medicine, it does not go against the intention of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that gold cautery is more subtle than iron, and they do not say that fire is better, but only by the quality of the gold and its fineness; and they say that the leaves of gold do not burn, but this is not true, for I have seen it happen in many people; and gold cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed when you burn the instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is charred by the color of the gold, and when it has cooled; and if you burn it too much, it will be charred by the fire; and there will be enough hindrance.</start_of_turn>
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have often observed in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter from the head down to the feet, because in this way it is easier to see it
dou cautere olivaire	the olive cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two things that cause them: a disease called “soda,” and many humors that descend from the head causing swelling of the eyes, ears, and the like.  There are also many dreams and pains of the teeth and throat, and even many diseases that come from the cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a medicinal solution modifying the head, either twice or thrice, according to what is useful and agreeable and accustomed to the patient; and then repeat the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his belly; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his elbow between his two fingers; and there or will come your two means, if it bleeds from the inside then evacuate the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take out the sign of ink, and make descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then keep your hand steadily, and renew the cautery until you see the bone somewhat; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that take up one-tenth of a spoonful of aloe, and put it on and cover with cotton wool, and take out the wound, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft dressing.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders say, the more time the wound is left open, the more it purges; and for this reason it is useful to apply pressure.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And the elders say, one must not leave the burn cautery on for too long, lest part of the bone should burn; then one must rese that which is around the bone, and it must be healed.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the elders say, one must not leave the burn cautery on for too long, lest part of the bone should burn; then one must rese that which is around the bone, and it must be healed.  One must also keep the wound open for a long time; after this it must be cured and dressed.</start_of_turn
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be of any benefit in all bones, except in certain homes or where there is doubt; and I believe that I must leave it alone; for the head of the shoulder is easily damaged by continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other limbs; and even when the patient’s condition is feeble by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more effective and gentler for me, and for this reason I will abstain from it.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head there is chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient must be given rest and drugs that are called «cochie», and vomiting of the head and oil and poultices; and if we make the cautery as we have said before, it is of no use.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that if the patient’s ailment is of great nature, and that it is not too painful; then the cautery should be made as we have said previously.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After having made the cautery on the bone of the head as we have said, and having made the cautery of the vein which is called the «vasselz», which is under the skin where we put the sponges; keep your hand still so that you do not see blood until you reach the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is better that the cautery be made on the corners than on the middle of the head, for this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the shoulder there is sudden pain, and the disease is prolonged, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by means of medicines, and other treatments have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this has availed nothing: then make cautery as I have said before, namely by means of medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of medicine is like this: if you take a dose of alum, and burn the skin and cover it. If there are two bones, then do the temple or the place where the pain remains in order to be able to reattach the dose of alum to the skin; and when it is reattached, if you bind and constrain it well and leave it for .xij. hours; and then take it off and treat the wound for .ij. days or .iij.; and put on a bandage as before until the swelling subsides.

de emigraine	De Emigraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When the armpit is cauterized as we have previously mentioned in the discussion of diseases, and it does not yield, and you see that the burn precedes the medicine and does not suffice, then it is necessary to abandon the cautery which is called the "knife" while it is still soft; and sign the limb with a line half an inch long, and hold the hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that life does not depart until the bone; and be careful of the jaw that is mute when you move it, and that the blood does not clot except for the spasm and tension that arise from the disease; and be careful of excessive bleeding from the artery when it is cauterized, or from the cautery itself which often causes great pain and even to those who are unskilled and inexperienced. de la torture de la bouche	From the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners. de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy.

Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hair grow large and even, then make a parchment like the shape of the laurel leaf; then take French soap and live salt, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it boil rapidly, if it does not freeze, then apply it upon the shape that you have made like the laurel leaf, and put on the papere eggs; and if the patient holds in one oil only, if you must open in one, and if in both; and put on the cotton oil soaked in egg white. And let the patient's arm be steady and put your hand showing on the medicine, and press it once and let it move every time the patient feels a biting of the medicine, for he feels a biting like of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, if the medicine has reached your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bite has passed, if you lift the limb up, and you see the wound rise just as if it had been raised by the contraction of fire or by incision; and if it is firm, it is well. If not, if you repeat the treatment on the limb or the treatment has not been effective, until your works are even and your wounds are at a point; then put on a moist compress over the wound until the sparks have ceased, and then cure the wound which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If you have taken great care of your work and there is no need for further medicine, and the wound becomes soft after the bite, and the hair is pricked with oil; then repeat the treatment on the limb which is softened by the oil, as you did before; then cure until it is healed. This is the form of a wound that has been treated with oil.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	Know that the spirits of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to this be their constraints; and do not be afraid to reply to him in the right way to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the healing of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cure does not help, then you must cauterize according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to hold their head still; and grasp their hair between your hands in a firm manner so that it does not move; after that, put a cotton swab moistened with oil or vinegar on the wound; then heat the cautery which is partly burnt: and hold it to the hair if it forms like a pine cone; gather the hair that it is burnt; if you see that some hair is pulled out from one root to the other, and if you see that there is as much as with a try; but in any case, this is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula until it is over, and draining the pus, and drying; and if it is closed, if the wound has healed, and drain the pus; then put the cautery on the wound, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part where there is no oil, so that your hands do not make a mess; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and compress it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you begin the cautery from the outset until the bone, that would be well. If this does not suffice, restart the cautery once more; if you are in doubt, leave it for two days. Then place a moist cotton swab in the wound and treat the desiccation until it is healed. If twenty days pass and it is still not healed, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow the advice of your physician.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	There is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients have mentioned. When there is a fistula, open the wound; then insert one inch of soft sponge into the opening in the following form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And one makes for the quantity of a third of a pound; and keep your hand or sponge firmly closed, and do not move the patient in any way, except the melted sponge comes out by itself; and it is necessary to put on the patient a moist cotton swab in the place of oil, wool or awl: the sponge if it is like that will come out from the fistula itself and will leave the remainder perfectly preserved and whole.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. But if this does not suffice, if it is necessary, it is permitted to perform a perforation on the nerve and bring the fistula back to its original place as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. But if this does not suffice, if it is necessary, it is permitted to perform a perforation on the nerve and bring the fistula back to its original place as it should be in its proper place.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. But if this does not suffice, if it is necessary, it is permitted to perform a perforation on the nerve and bring the fistula back to its original place as it should be in its proper place

Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated these fractures as we have said in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you should perform a small burn cautery as follows:
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the armpit of the arm</start_of_turn
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the armpit of the arm or the elbow or the shoulder or the root of the tooth comes loose, after making a perforation and rounding it off and it becomes swollen and forms a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the sections, and it does not help: therefore you must make a burn cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after making the hole or opening the fistula, and keep your hand as long as it takes for life to return to its place; or behind the limb; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is sound; and if it is cured once, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	Pain du mouvement des dents
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have cured it with medicines and that does not suffice, then put the patient’s head in your hand; after remove the cautery whose form will come afterwards in this way as if you were putting on a pincer on the tooth; and put the cautery into the tooth cavity immediately, and hold your hand as long as the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after let go of your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and spit out the water.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth which was moving is confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the moisture corrupts dries out.
de la dolor des dens	Of toothache.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical treatments are of no avail, then there must be recourse to cautery in two ways: cautery of the carbuncle and cautery of the fire.</start_of_turn>
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of the carbuncle is like this: take burnt barley and grind it to a powder; take a spoonful of the powder and place it on the tip of a rag, and moisten the bottom of the toothache with saliva; hold the toothache firmly in the barley until it is cold; and do this until the root of the tooth is softened.  When you see that the barley is limp and the cotton is wet, put the toothache back in place and put the iron on the tooth until the fire has died down at the bottom of the tooth.</start_of_turn
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Cautery of the fire is like this: take a crucible of iron or charcoal, and make it big enough so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery until it is red hot, and hold it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cold; do this often, for the pain will be almost as great from the burning as from the toothache itself.  And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with much saliva in the course of this cautery, and then spit; for this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make cautery of whatever part you wish, and as you please; and that is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	And make cautery of whatever part you wish, and as you please; and that is the form of the burn.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When carbuncles are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not subject to digestion by medicines, then it is necessary to burn away the cautery beforehand as it comes to pass; for there are often several openings from the fumes to reach the cautery of the other part. And put the cautery hot upon the abscess once, or twice as much as the mixture will bear; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery on according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in for two days; and put upon moist cotton wool around it until the soreness is gone.  Then cure the wound of abscesses and tensions until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the wind and cold, then it is fitting that the patient be relieved first by soluble medicines; afterwards perform the cautery at the root of the jaw, and hold it until you reach the jaw without causing further pain. Afterwards perform another cautery at the junction of the neck and the spine, and let the cautery which is called the "clamp" remain in place; and cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	When moisture prevails over the wind and cold, then it is fitting that the patient be relieved first by soluble medicines; afterwards perform the cautery at the root of the jaw, and hold it until you reach the jaw without causing further pain. Afterwards perform another cautery at the junction of the neck and the spine, and let the cautery which is called the "clamp" remain in place; and cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed.

When all and diseases of the wind are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or sweating, and is an ancient disease, if you perform two cauteries on the forcele in their veins; and another cautery between two vertebrae; and let the cautery which is called the "clamp" remain in place as it is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see it, perform cautery at its point throughout which the cautery is named "points" for it forms thus in the disease of the ears; and let the points be done up to .xxx., or as much as necessary. After curing the limb according to what is above said, and let the cautery be done twice as many times as this form indicates.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason the cautery is lighter, for this reason that you do it twice as many times as before.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, hold the patient’s shoulders and chest; then take the thumb which is inside the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is loosened, if it has slipped out of place, if it is showing, withdraw the cautery which is just as wide as the nail of the index finger:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and burn the thumb until it reaches the chest, and comes the escape of the cautery all together three times; for this is done with the cautery which has two nails, because the figures of cautery are these two nails; and the nerves are in proportion to the fineness of the attempt and this is the form of the cautery which has two nails.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is the suture placed upon this nerve for there are six cauteries there.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the cautery over the broiled boils with silk; then rest the patient and do not allow the limb to hang tense for too long as to cause discomfort.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if there is displacement below, whatever the cause, then make a cautery over the callous of the cautery staple, or several cauteries by pricking. For the joint is closed and the moisture is solidified and the patient is cured.</start_of_turn
dou cautere de pleuresin	because of the wound of the cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that we must make for tears the cauteries of the root of Aristotle, and in part manner: take a root of Aristotle long, the greatest that thou shalt find, and dry, and as thick and as long as thy thumbs; and moisten in oil, and stamp at the fire, and cauterize. I. Cauterize between the forcele and the collarbone, and II. A few cauteries one at a distance in the part which is below the beard; and III. Cauterize between the fifth costal cartilage and the rib, declining behind one at a distance. I. Cauterize over the testicle, and I. another upon the stomach, and I. between two ribs, and I. two costae from the testis which oppose the cautery which is between two ribs; and do not press me thy hand, but make it open as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And they say no ancient man uses a fire cautery resembling a razor, and throws it and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to this incision; and they leap forth from pain, as we have said in the incision of the liver. de la mice	of mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse of what we have said about the divisions of the cures, and it brings no profit, then there remain two methods of cautery which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	When you treat the disease of the mouse of what we have said about the divisions of the cures, and it brings no profit, then there remain two methods of cautery which are good.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and another method of cautery if it is that you burn off the nerve which has twelve nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and hold the limb where the mouse is, or the patient’s shoulder comes toward the left side, and elevate the limb which you bind to the limb, according to the length of the bone, and burn according to the size of the bone.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. After that, if the burn is not inflamed as much as the kernel is perceived from the other side, then take out the cautery and leave three. And if you see that the burn has progressed to the entirety of the burn, take out two hairs. After that, cure as soon as it has grasped by long tension, and thus is it as good as the other cures that have been said.
de ydropisie	After that, if the burn is not inflamed as much as the kernel is perceived from the other side, then take out the cautery and leave three. And if you see that the burn has progressed to the entirety of the burn, take out two hairs. After that, cure as soon as it has grasped by long tension, and thus is it as good as the other cures that have been said.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The cautery is not worth as much as an ipecacanth treatment, except for the manner which is called “asclytes”. When you treat according to the methods that we have said in the divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make three cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two at the back on the spine, and one in the buttock; and that the cautery be placed very close to the hair root.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to stop the bleeding, do not leave the wound closed in the patient after the cautery; rather, let healing haste, and they will be bound together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the belly cautery is like a nail that we have before us; and the back is olive-shaped, as is seen here.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the pieces

de la menoison	After having made two incisions in the thigh, cauterize the area around the knee; let the cauteries be long, one above the kneecap and the other below, in the middle of the thigh; leave the cauteries in place for a while, that they may adhere; then perform the other treatments that we have mentioned.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches. Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make the fire cautery on the navel, that is, cauterize on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make the fire cautery on the navel, that is, cauterize on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are deep-seated or multiple, and have been present for a long time, and are composed of thick, cold, and moist humors, they are cured as we have said in the divisions; and it is of no use to make cauteries: that is, two on the spine of the back, which is quite sufficient to drive away all the pain of the hemorrhoids, and two on the buttocks. The latter two should be made immediately;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you think the stomach is cold, and the meat is not cooked, and the face is swollen, then the face must be subjected to a great cautery on the stomach, as it is said above; and another on the liver, and another on the spleen throughout the entire cautery clamp; and leave the cautery open for a long time. After that, cure the limb until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	If you think the stomach is cold, and the meat is not cooked, and the face is swollen, then the face must be subjected to a great cautery on the stomach, as it is said above; and another on the liver, and another on the spleen throughout the entire cautery clamp; and leave the cautery open for a long time. After that, cure the limb until it is healed.
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you feel the thelul, if you withdraw the cautery which appears to burn, and then put it all ablaze on that thelul which is grasped; and leave it until the blood vessel comes to birth, without tension; do this once or twice. And if there is much thelul, if you cauterize each as we have said; after that, cure the wound with useful remedies until it is healed; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on the belly, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	From an unhealed wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure pain or opening, as we have said, if there is some disease which can only be cured by cautery, then
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no fistula, and it is inflamed and discharges pus and moisture, if the physician desires to attempt a cure, and keeps that he will extract the foreign matter at all costs. After having evacuated the cautery which appears to have burned away, insert it into the fistula according to the degree of the attempt which has been made; and repeat the cautery until the burned and corrupted parts are gone, once or twice or thrice; take care of the nerves which are nearby and of the large veins. If the fistula is close to the bladder or intestine, take care of these organs as well, and do not do more than is necessary; and think that it is not always necessary to do this. After curing the wound until it is healed, if the foreign matter has been removed, and the tissues are tense, then extract the foreign matter; if the foreign matter is not ossified, extract it when the wound is healed, and corrupt it at the same time; and do the same as we have said concerning this matter.
de la maladie des reins	De la maladie des reins.
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the flanks comes with swelling and great wind, and does not take nourishment from a woman, then it is necessary to cauterize the kidneys from one side to the other with the cautery needle which we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, if there are two cauteries in a line, it will bring more relief.</start_of_turn>
de la vessie	Of the bladder.
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is full and weak of fruit and moisture, and the patient holds back urine, then one should cauterize on the lower part of the bladder, where the hair begins to grow, both towards the belly and towards the flanks, and make as many cauteries as there are pores; and one should also cauterize the back, or if necessary, the needle should be passed through the navel.
de la marris	De la marris.
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow me to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings are late; and when they come, if they cause great pain: then it is advisable to make two cauteries around the knee, as we said before, or a cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries of the buttocks; or let the cautery be applied to the navel, as we said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the hip socket, and because of this the limb moves differently, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the hip joint is painful, if you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket like a circle, and sign in front of the limb around the socket if it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and if the cautery is made like this as we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cautery treatments are not present, make two olive-shaped cautery burns, and let the cautery be as strong as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	And if these cautery treatments are not present, make two olive-shaped cautery burns, and let the cautery be as strong as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the previous section, and the cure is not lasting, and the disease is old: therefore it is advised that you purge the patient of the foul humors through foul pills, or other solid pills that resemble them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the manner after the fire cautery is as follows: it is to say with an assembly of medicines and fire cautery. Fire cautery is as follows: for example, you cauterize upon the hip bone twice; you make three triangular cauteries as this, and you do it to a great depth and breadth, and there is between each cauterization an interval equal to the thickness of an olive, or the like. Never do you make a cautery in the middle of the head of the femur, for there are three of them according to this fashion.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that you have cauterized around the circle that we have said concerning the dislocation of the hip; but do it partly cautiously that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the thickness of the thigh is taut.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. And this is how it is done in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, you make three cauteries there or the patient says that the pain is there, and one cauterization under the ankle bone three times, on the left side one; and the cautery is either blunt or with a needle; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up to two fingers or almost as much, you cauterize at the place where the pain is felt twice or three times at the cauterization called the "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If the shoulder joint is stiff, make it more flexible; if the pain persists from the elbow to the hip, make an incision with the cautery knife, either straight or circular, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery too long, nor burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient any greater pain or contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I have seen many others who have cauterized the ankle bone without removing the spur, and left it so long that the limb was completely limp, and they were pricked through and through, and the whole limb was perforated and corrupted. After this there was death of the belly
