This is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the hair grow until it is all red and thick, and then put it on the patient’s thigh; and let the burn slowly over the skin; and burn once. Repeat the burn and leave it for two days. Then make an ointment of butter, and leave the wound open long and tight; after the cure of the wound while it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that our physicians often use this cautery because of its bad reputation, and that we often see those who use it; and all these are scorched bones, which can suffer from it, and where he takes care of himself.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes from the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things of cold expanding matter, none of these symptoms is worth cautery, save for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is free from foul pills or other similar things, that we make on his back, there or where the pain is, three lines signed with a needle, and in a fourth line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small swelling, and its signs are that when it swells it hurts the loin and causes fear; and you find it behind the lower spine on the back and its appearance comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle according to this form. If it is necessary to cauterize some part of the spine, and if you see it, if you cauterize around the spine at the cautery marking one or two lines, and keep the points close to one another. After curing the limb until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring about further cautery in a hasty manner that is in vain of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain comes from a piece that is called "podagre" properly, and when the cause is cold and treated by medicines, it cannot be cured; if it is cured by cautery in part: make the mouth of the cautery enter the joint at the point of pain, and let the cautery be of the olive kind according to this fashion:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	When there is need to prick the face of the limb, if you make the cautery throughout the whole area, call it "point". And if the pains come up to the joints and there are others, which often happens, make the cautery on each joint twice or thrice on each side, with the whole olive cautery; and if you must do more, if you make more, but do not keep your hand far from the fire until the thickness of the hair is as much as the beard.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains go down to the joints and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, if you make pricks around the nail twice. And if there is no longer any pain, if you make pricks on some joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the buttocks or the shoulder blades, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient govern himself well and take medicine. For if you make him govern himself and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	From the root of the scapula.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a fracture approaches the shoulder, and the ball comes loose as new, if you wish to cure it, do not break off the limb; and do use things that leave the belly open, so that the pain may go down from the belly; afterwards let him sit on his buttocks between your hands, and command him to hold his arm tight until the bone is healed, and keep it firm at your sides, and mark on the skin above the collarbone the extent of the fracture, and do all that is like half a circle below the bone. Then withdraw the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	... until it is soft and limp. Then reattach the ball to its place; and the minister should hold his hand so that it does not recoil; and provide good sutures for the patient, and put some lint and some thread on the wound, and another on his wrist; then place the cautery on the mark on his whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you have fixed the bone, and if you do not succeed the first time, if you start again until you reach the bone; and beware diligently that the ball does not slip while you are making the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this means the patient does not die, or any other mishap.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And if you do not come up to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. It is necessary that the cauteries of small people be subtle in measure, and those of great people also great in measure; after two days, cure the burn until the scab is bony; after that, cure other ailments until they are healed, and keep the patient forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and make sure that his movements are lazy so that he does not bleed when he moves to his bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	After forty days, when he wants to rise, let him be accompanied by a well-made staff and keep him for forty days; and give him good rest, that he work little and abstain from drinking too much wine and eating too much, and from excessive laughter; and when he has followed this teaching, if he is well, he will be entirely healed. And I will tell you afterwards about the treatment of your ailment in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the treatment of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When routes come into other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, then make a second cautery according to their quantity, and a third of the dose; after which treat according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at two angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	...there is no greater pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or ailment, and the pain persists for a long time, medical treatment is of no avail; therefore, it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery known as the "poins," or with a cautery according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, its toughness and its tortures, and its pain. If successful in the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure once more for it is customary to effect the cauteries as close to the diseased part as possible, so that the pain is relieved while the disease is still present.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or ailment, and the pain persists for a long time, medical treatment is of no avail; therefore, it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery known as the "poins," or with a cautery according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, its toughness and its tortures, and its pain. If successful in the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure once more for it is customary to effect the cauteries as close to the diseased part as possible, so that the pain is relieved while the disease is still present.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The moisture is never of any avail by cautery; great aid is only obtained from it when dealing with the initial stages of disease caused by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see the disease being cauterized, take care that the disease is in its early stages; if it is cured according to what has been said in the division, and if it does not linger, you may doubt that the corruption has spread throughout the whole disease; therefore, make five cauteries on the head: one at the nape of the neck, and the other toward the front at the end of the beard; two on the two corners, and one behind the earlobe; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries are in progress until the bones are reached, and as long as the surrounding humors escape through the incisions, so that the vapors of the bad humors can escape. Cauterize the head according to what is seen before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If the mess is scattered everywhere; and it appears manifestly, if you must indeed cauterize with these cauteries which we have spoken of or chief, namely the cautery in some places you desire not to, and two cauteries on the armpits, and three on the spine of the neck, and one great on the hip and one other from below, and two on the two scapulae, and two on the flanks, and two on the tendons of the wrist and elbow, and one on almost every joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; take heed of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and in no way perform cautery on the bone of the heel or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	When you make more cauteries, the more you do to aid, and the more you profit from it; and when the patients do not feel pain from the cautery, as they would if they were healthy, because their flesh is already corrupted. And you must know that the cauteries should be great and small according to the limbs and joints, as you do in handling herbs. After treatment with flour of several times with honey and other treatments until they are healed.
de enfleure	of swelling.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not entirely healed, then you must make cauteries on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either make the cauteries a little deeper than the depth of the nerve that moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And never make a cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of a nerve that moves the limb, and so if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything be interposed that does not know the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves from the bones.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not entirely healed, then you must make cauteries on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either make the cauteries a little deeper than the depth of the nerve that moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And never make a cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of a nerve that moves the limb, and so if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything be interposed that does not know the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves from the bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then you must make a cautery with a needle a little deep, according to the depth of the tissue, until the swelling is bony and has changed color; then cure with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it in place until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre first begins, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery that seems like a circle, put all around the circumference of the chancre. And everyone says that it should be cauterized in the middle of the chancre; however, I do not think that is good because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it is better to cauterize around the circumference, at the circle cautery, as we have said in our teaching of cautery.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati", and it lingers without healing or because of excessive swelling that the patient makes or because of the weight of the ailment when it is decrepit (that is, too great), and there is much blood, or for fear; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it alone. For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turning pale with all the cautery, if it is hot, take away the cautery for a moment: thus is the shape
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries perceive the heat, and be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in part as the disease progresses. After that cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The fire cautery. Instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the wounds that come from the heel to the toe.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece of flesh has departed from its place, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome thing that boils up like the scum of the earth. And the cautery of this disease is in two ways. Namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that which is done by the eschaufleur; that is, the cautery is made like a pennace of a nail, and is done with a piece of iron of the measure that it can penetrate the abscess of all parts, and that there are subtle margins; after this put all around the abscess, and hold your hand firmly over the abscess until it comes to the front of the abscess; and leave it like this for two days until it begins to discharge pus; then make an poultice of bruised mallow seeds with gum, and leave the poultice on all night, and close the abscess firmly and will be drained of its roots. Then cure the wound by applying char until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by boils in the hands and in pieces, if you must bring them to the surface, do the hot water cautery; and this is in part as follows: take a splinter of flax or iron, or a nail of pitch, and put it on the abscess and the dressing; that is, make incisions around the edges; and put the splinter on so that it reaches all around, then put on some warm oil, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the splinter comes to the root of the abscess, and can find the hot water going deep to the root; and give the patient a sip of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will discharge all its roots. Do this again and again until you have drained all that is in the abscess, and then cure the wounds that have resulted from the char.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shiver from cold, or from a quartan fever or from any other, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will soon recover from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When some shiver from cold, or from a quartan fever or from any other, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will soon recover from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever the body is covered in boils, or pus-filled abscesses, that come from corrupt matters, if you make a cautery on each head of the abscess at the first appearance: a subtle cautery of fir tree ash, from which the point should be grasped by the fire, or of elderberry root long, or the lenticular cautery. And never should the abscesses be cauterized before they appear, according to this method, for they will not burst forward, but the superflux from which they come is broken, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there are often great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend oneself.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you are hasty to put your finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it out too much without calming it down, and blood does not stop flowing; then take away several small and large olive cauteries as soon as they are red, and touch them to the wound, that is, great or small as is appropriate for the wound and the limb in which the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your finger there, and hold the cautery as long as necessary.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts blood when you take your finger away from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hold of another cautery quickly that is on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the limb is completely stretched out; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is below, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and stretch the limb until, without drawing blood from the artery, it can be satisfactorily restored to its normal position, except in three ways that we have mentioned: or by cautery, or by extraction when necessary, or by strong ligation with thread, or by medicines that are placed upon it and which have power to restore blood flow.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about a restoration of the limb by means of tight draping or of placing things burning upon it, or other similar things, will not profit thereby unless he does so in the right way.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to be the case and there is no remedy or medicine present, he must place his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still until it is restored beneath the wound and beneath the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is cold as much as the limb is frozen and engrosed and restored; and make incisions in front of those which must be cauterized and medicated.</start_of_turn>
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This text is not included in the requested translation, as it is not provided in the input.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that in all diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or apply burning medicine, we must inquire into the omens, causes, instruments, and shapes of the cauteries; and in this chapter we will speak of the chief matters that we have found to be lighter in this way than in others.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, although I begin this chapter, it is necessary, my son, to teach you that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first cauteries, and for this reason more caution is required.</start_of_turn
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.</start_of_turn
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not be rash. For many people come to healing in various ways. If they come from those who have suffered greatly with their ailment and who move easily through the force of their ailment, and from the greatness of their malice; of these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are some who will tell you, "Wait, I am ready"; and the ailment is grievous. It is not right that you should yield only to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not be rash more than wisely in what you are certain of, and what you have learned; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is either saved or transformed; and this will help you to achieve good fame, glory, and memory forever.</start_of_turn>
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords teach you to understand and fear, and if you are filled with the spirit of the Holy Inspiration of his hand, amen.</start_of_turn>
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordonné cet chapitre en divisant par Chapitre, selon ce qui est devant ou Chapitre des cauteres, que I vos ai devisé de la tête jusqu’à la pied, pour ce que vous trouvez plus facilement ce que vous avez à faire.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered this chapter by dividing into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the foot, so that you can find more easily what you have to do.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	The disease comes out of the belly of women in childbirth, and when the boy cries too much the head of the child is strained; and never comes from a known cause except that it is not treated.</start_of_turn>
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have never seen such a disease as this except in childhood, when the head of the shoulder was completely swollen with fluid, and the bone grew so much that it could not support itself; and I thought that the moisture was too great, and this moisture, if it is gathered on the bone above the scapula, between the shoulder blade and the bone; and the work is like this if the moisture is between the shoulder blade and the bone, and the incision is small, that you must make a wide incision; and it should be as long as.ij. we, until the moisture is gone. And when this is done, the shape of the scapula will be like that of a spindle.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make.ij. incisions in the manner of a cross, following this shape:

After the incision, draw out the moisture forcefully. Another method of incision is to look or open the abscess, and gather the pus; for it is never before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.

Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus is the method of extracting them [arrows] that if the patient make retreat the hairs from his temples, and understand to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is often returned full rather than in other men who are too rough; and if it is returned, the patient must stretch his neck with some folds, then wipe the limb of any rough scab, and rise the limb of warm water until the artery opens manifestly; then take the sponge which is like this shape:

And thus is the method of extracting them that if the patient makes retreat the hairs from his temples, and understands to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is often returned full rather than in other men who are too rough; and if it is returned, the patient must stretch his neck with some folds, then wipe the limb of any rough scab, and rise the limb of warm water until the artery opens manifestly; then take the sponge which is like this shape: then gently stretch the leather until you see the artery, then pull it up with tweezers, and remove it well from the cloths that are soaked with blood from the chest; and if the artery is fragile, if the head of the bone is fractured, then break the head of that part according to the quantity of blood spilled. For if it is not broken, it will not jump out without pain throughout.

Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is useful to extract the arteries when they are filled with much cotton and held in well-made bands; and when they are released, if they are cured with dry medicines that cause the hair to grow, and the bands, until they are healed; and if you do not have the artery held in place as you ought, if you are in a hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use vinegar in the hand that is holding it, it will stain; and if you do not have that, if you must remove the hand, you must do so while it is still warm, and wash the hand with cold water until it stops bleeding, and hold it steady as you should; and what is more gentle and easier in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery at the depth of a third, but the depth should be well spaced in order to prevent the heat from lasting too long.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tense, it holds less heat.

This is the form of the cautery:

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the old 'cure contuse'. si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and is very well cut on one side, and on the other is smooth, do not cut deeply, and this is its form:

If in the first fissure the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and is very well cut on one side, and on the other is smooth, do not cut deeply. And place the cutting edge towards the cartilage at the shoulder, and the smooth edge towards the bone, and hold tight until it reaches the middle fissure. And remove all the blood vessels that descend from the head as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the shoulder, and then do the same in the middle of the fissure until it reaches the other edge; and then draw out the blood equally, express the wound for the blood taken; then put in the wound the dressing of a little cotton tent, and put on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and balsam, and keep that the stitches should not be visible; and at the end remove the ligature and insert a great number of stinging nettle leaves, then cure with basic ointment with rose oil, and other cures which are used for wounds, until it is healed.

Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute burning comes, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilate, and the papers burn; and the hair cries out, and where previously there was no pain, now there is great pain, and the patient expels; then it is certain that from these symptoms and the burning which comes from many veins, there is no other remedy except to cure the root of the matter.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And command the patient to rest his forehead, then make a great incision from the left temple to the right temple, and so on from the left side to the right.
