de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes swelling of the ears is among these things: grains, or pus, or stone or other foreign bodies like iron; or seeds, like peas, beans, or beans; or fluid-filled things like urine and saliva or other things.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear or in any other way that does not fit into the ear, do not put the ear up to the sun. If you see the stone, if no violet oil or oil of lavender comes out, then extract it; and let him spit out some mustard seeds, and stamp the nostrils when he spits, and put round the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear still. Many times this cure comes out by itself; and if it does not come out, it is necessary to extract it with fine needles, as is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, extract it with a fine needle of double curvature; and if it does not come out even with that, make an injection of ointment and cut off the top of the injection or break the ear very much, and stamp what is around the injection of ointment if it comes out and cannot enter with the needle; then the pain will cease, for often it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in part, take hold of the ear and put on no instrument that can cause injury, and put a little cloth over; then press the hold on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will cease.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things fail, if you are in haste to make an incision at the ear root or at the base of the jaw, and spasm, do as follows: make the first incision at the front of the head, and drain blood in accordance with its quantity. Then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fatty or bony prominence. Make the incision as wide as a crescent, until you reach the bone, and remove the pus promptly from your mouth. Continue the treatment until the wound is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is a grain that is ensnared and swells, administer extraction; if it cannot be extruded, administer a sponge held tightly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	If it is a grain that is ensnared and swells, administer extraction; if it cannot be extruded, administer a sponge held tightly according to this form: make an incision of that grain. But do not do this until you have made many attempts; then extract with forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In acute cases, when the ear aches, the patient must immediately apply pressure to the ear with the thumb and index finger, and fill the ear with cotton wool. And if the ear is still painful, do so while pressing on the ear itself or on the side of the ear; if that does not suffice, take many stones and press them along the length of the ear, keeping the thumb and index finger pressed to the ear; and remove the patient’s earwax with one hand and the stones with the other; and press one stone on the ear from the other side, and hold it down on the ear that is in the ear; and do not stop pressing the stones until the pain has entirely disappeared; and as soon as the pain has gone, remove the stones. If you see that the pain persists, take the thumb and index finger of the other hand and press one of the stones into the ear, and press the other stone with the thumb until the most intense pain has passed; then repeat the process with the other stones until the pain has entirely gone, as we have said concerning the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small size, like a flea and other small things, cure it as we have said in the preceding division; but if it is of large size, you can feel it; in such a case, extract the tooth. It is the easiest thing to remove that which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you have cured as we have said in the preceding division or performed distillations, and the cure has not been of benefit, if you wish to be certain, look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms visible, if there are only superficial scratches, and if there are none, take the tweezers which are of this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let the wound be broad and deep. And keep the upper part of the ear in proportion to the extent of the suffering of the patient, then proceed with the cautery; do this often until you see that all the smoke has escaped. And if they do not obey in this, if I press upon the edge of the cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not emerge forcefully as we have said, give distillations which the ancients have proved effective in the cutting of worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, this is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let the wound be of silver or gold, be it small losses, and above put on for distillation; and press from within the distillation with a well-made instrument of gold, as I have said, and if you see take a scraper and wrap around the point immediately cotton; then I pour out your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the can, and the can be in the ear; then put back the scraper on all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or almost all the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and let the distillation be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some hole in their ear; and the same thing happens at home through wound bursting or earwax being blocked in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see; and never happens without a certain degree of loss of hearing, which one sees very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When these bursts happen without being seen, they are a sign of serious illness in many cases, and in this case one sees that you put the painful ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation apparent, if the swelling has completely disappeared, this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it greasy or slimy before and behind all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the opilation is of pus or earwax, if you see little pinpricks, and the swelling is lighter, as long as the pus is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the swelling has penetrated the ear, take a fine needle and pierce a small hole in the ear, then put in an ear drop. If you feel the swelling which the patient feels in the ear, pierce slightly, and do not pierce the nerve of the ear; then put in the ear a patch according to the size of the hole, and the pus in the Egyptian manner.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do nothing more until the wound is healed; take a swab and mix it with rose-water and powdered vitriol; if you see the swelling flee the ear, it is likely that you have pulled out the swab. Put in another swab soaked in oil of roses and beeswax until the swelling is bony; then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is discharge of blood, soak a sponge and wring it out in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that will stop the bleeding such as applying distillations.</start_of_turn>
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	From the heap of papers
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decor, if the cautery of the lenticular scar is done without incision, and the cautery is done afterwards, it is worth moving; and many times it repairs itself, so that nothing remains of its root; and when they are cauterized by fire, if they are burned those roots and do not return again.
de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come papers with blood that seems to coagulate in its form and hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granulin," and is an assembly of large moisture in the substance of the wound; the work is like this: take warning if the granulin moves from one side to the other, and that is a light matter; then make a mark with the thumb and index finger, then grasp the wound firmly, and pull. If you do not pull it with force enough to see some blood, it will grieve the patient nothing; but if the wound is large, if the assembly has a support, and the cure as much as it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for it will heal itself quickly and leave a scar.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the granulin descends downwards towards the ear towards the upper part, reverse the wound, and bring the granulin to a few pinches; grasp and press from one side to the other; and if the wound is stripped by the incision, it will grieve nothing; and when the wound is closed, leave the dirty oil, and cure the limb of that which leaves a scar as long as the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the blood
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on papers of fine texture, and this is more effective for those who have no nails, and grieve much at their eyes, and they come out with tears at dawn, and they cannot bear the sight of the sun because their tears are too hasty at their eyes; and because they lie with their faces down, and sleep on their backs, and their papers are soaked with their tears which swell and appear covered in exinach which is released in oil. And when you press their limbs and feel the exinach between their toes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	When the patient puts his head in order; then take one drape of linen, and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from the chest part, and put it on; and press on the thumbs from one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the tip of the knife a wound not larger than the wound made to the vein; and make the skin taut as long as you see the exinach; and in various situations comes exinach from the wound, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tissue from the piece of cartilage between your thumbs at the back, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not bring together in the wound, that you do not reach the whole thickness just until the oil, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it escapes not at the beginning of the incision, if you expand a little the incision lightly until it opens; then draw it out as we have said, and moisten the edges with oil and water, and put on the limb, and strain it gently.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who break their bones and put on them to support the moisture that is gone. Then cure them until they are healed. And if it comes to the limb again with swelling, if you cure abscesses that swell up until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like tissues grow hair-like bristles other than their natural state, and are thickened, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases such as tears, and softening of the paper-like tissues and mucus, as well as the destruction of the hairs; and the cure for this is in three ways: either by whole-body cautery with fire, or by means of water medicine as I have said, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient’s hand over your left hand; if the paper changes, that is good; if not, if there is an awl with a single thread at the root of the hair; whether you cut the edge of the paper or the hair sprouts from these hairs, take a single thread from the root of the hair to the tip of the paper, and stretch it out; then pull out the hair from the root, from the root of the bristles to the tip of the nail; then draw out the single thread, and put on the paper a small patch of cotton and bandage, and mark on the paper a sign like the mark of a thrush, and know that the sign must be in accordance with the quantity of the paper that you see being lifted that is required for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is much paper that has been softened in any part, then make at least two lines from the sign you have made; from the great nail to the little one; and if there is an opening near the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then close the opening in one of the two angles of the knee, then pull out all the hair; then gather the two layers together with a suture of a fine thread of wool, and wipe off the blood, and make air the excess of threads on the two edges of everything you have glued, as you see; and if you do not see this, do not cure, but leave the suture and the threads for two or three days; then cure the wound with something dry and constricting, because the paper returns to its place under the wound and the gathering of the two layers, but the suture is useless (as the old people say), and this is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another manner: if you mark the mark of a figure that is just like the head of a myrtle, as we have said, at that point two needles must be drawn out following the shape that is there.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold together that which is above with small forces equally following the shape that is there.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the nails, and the thing is not even, if you take a needle or there is a thread, and you pass it through the mark; and you pass another thread from above the great scar, and the second thread from below the small one, and you assemble between your two the two threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the skin above where you have marked, as we have said, then assemble the two layers of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply cerate and other soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hairs of the beard are converted: if you use what we have said about incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard and the hair inwards as I have said, then make four incisions by art, and four fine threads as long as the beard and the diameter of a hazelnut; and put in four hairs or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other firmly on that which rests on the oil of the beard; strain the four incisions from the four parts forming; and leave it so for several days, and the skin which has been strained will become pale and wrinkled and will swell, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, if the beard has fallen out, it will not prick again; and this is the form of the four incisions that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a fine needle, and there is inside it a thread of silk fine and subtle; then assemble the hairs and do not knot one with the other subtly, and let the length of the thread be as long as a palm; then command in the chase another thread subtle of silk briefly, and do not knot the chief with the thread; then put the patient's chief in your hand; and let go of the sun if the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and light work, then withdraw the needle at all the chase in the root of the hair which grows naturally; then pull out the hair until it breaks at the root as much as you pull out naturally; then draw out the hand as much as the vein escapes at all the chase in the palm with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have commanded, until the chase vein comes out from under and you see it through the vision of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair comes back to its place and the burden is gone.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called 'aleacrati' or the inflammation comes to the head, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it comes from an abscess, or from a wound or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to work in this is that you make this suture, dry the flesh of it, put inside some threads of linen, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything else except use things that dry and tighten. For if you do that, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there is need for soft things, like fennel; and the rose of aquilegia or elderberry and flaxseed should be boiled, and aquilon ointment should be melted in none of the oils, and it should cover a bandage, and it should be cured like this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the form it had before; and this work that we have said is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fire that comes from the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is known as scaldure which really is apeled "axacrati", is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and fissure and cautery and things which are similar; and the way of this ailment is that if you take a needle, because it has two threads, and the thread is in the oil, and it causes the left eye to shed tears so that the thread of the vein is in two pieces at the end of the needle, and the thread is above the skin at the whole of the needle, and the head has one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound comes back as it should, that is good; if not, take a needle and put it in the wound, and rotate the wound, and make two incisions or break through twice the thickness of the wound; and let two angles be made at the two ends of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are reunited, the limb should look like the letter that has not "j griesche"; then break that bone, according to the quantity of cost and moisture, of what is in the wound, then join the two broken ends, and bind with a thread of linen; then cure from what we have said of the mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the ailment comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is known that there is hair loss from papery substances, and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be carried out according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know everything better than I do concerning the return of the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him and the instruments in more numerous positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the ailment comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is known that there is hair loss from papery substances, and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be carried out according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know everything better than I do concerning the return of the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him and the instruments in more numerous positions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stiffness arises at home in part as the limb above is soothed with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if it is known that the bone has been fractured, then it must be bled from the point of a scraper from below the bone, and held up high; and the edges must be bound as tightly as possible, without causing excessive pain, for the patient cannot endure too much pain or excessive bleeding; and the incision, which you have made, must be slight, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and all that is assembled must be thoroughly cleansed, and no longer washed in salted water, but with fresh water, and oil; and between the bone and the oil put a bandage of lint, and cover the oil with coarse wool in abundance; and after that apply a support as much as is necessary until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The fennel oil has two kinds: one is nervous and somewhat dark like pitch, and the other is not nervous but is like pale moisture that solidifies when touched by iron and becomes black like soot; both of them begin to soften towards the great marrow, and grow so much that they cover the whole cavity and the brightness and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And as for the incision, if the patient places his head in its right place, then hold the eyes; then grasp the hair with your hand, then take a needle and make a small incision at the root of the hair; insert one hair of a horse, or of a sheep, or of a bull, and a strong thread; double the point of the needle once and pass the needle through the hair, and grasp the hair with the thread and pull it out, and with all the hair surrounding the root that surrounds the nail and the hair to the root, then cut away all the superfluous tissue until only a little bit of the natural oil remains; and if there is no other discharge from the incision, do not extend the incision alone, but with the thread as we have said; then stretch out the surrounding tissue as much as possible.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fatty tissue and breaks it, and that the needle is not perceived; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of bruised salve, and apply a bandage, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread does not go in, many times this semblance of a nail of medicine is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you pour oil on the patient, and take the spatula lightly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gradually, and if you see that it has diminished point and the wound is pressing, if you distill from your mouth into the oil bandage make of alum and red salve, and bruise the salve, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other operation according to this same operation, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk first and cure the abscess thoroughly while it is sound, then repeat the work as before, while it is sound.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If there appears in the oil at night a piece of soft tissue that causes great swelling, if you suspend it on an onion and cut off a part and not all, that blood does not arise; then distill in the red oil of colera which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the plumule.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are never red with anger, and cover the pupils and hold them tight with paper; and appear like a rosebud. And if the patient puts his head in his bosom, then he covers the eyes, and all that colour is left with a convenient amount of yellow, and the colour is strong; then he severs the first colour, and goes on severing until the end, and he keeps only the white of the eye at the work; and let the incision be deep as the incision of the vein and have little force, as it is shown after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	When the incision is complete and all the colour is gone, if you use sesame oil bruised or you distill collyrium red and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil cotton with a little egg white, so that it is firmly fixed; and if it does not stop, and the patient vomits, and you doubt the depth of the incision, if you leave the oil and cure the abscess with soothing things. Then return to your work when it is healed, and then do the incisions again when the colours are added to the oil in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But always know that you should temper the treatment with a weak oil of natural origin; and by chance, in the work of iron; and do not move your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	Des voines des eulz.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The veins of the eyes.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	Red veins covered with oil, tolerate the gaze of the eye and expel the oil throughout the days. The surgeon must therefore be the first to notice if the oil is strong; for there is no other disease more violent than a wound; therefore the surgeon should act immediately: instruct the patient to put his head in a normal position, then suspend those veins to the utmost extent of his skill, and do so discreetly in the following manner:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Red veins covered with oil, tolerate the gaze of the eye and expel the oil throughout the days. The surgeon must therefore be the first to notice if the oil is strong; for there is no other disease more violent than a wound; therefore the surgeon should act immediately: instruct the patient to put his head in a normal position, then suspend those veins to the utmost extent of his skill, and do so discreetly in the following manner: discreetly suspend those veins without causing any pain, and let the blood drain out afterwards; do this work at midday when the sun is shining, and be wary of any spasms.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot bear all this in that hour, make an ointment from oil and soothing things to soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pain is appeased and the swelling has subsided; then repeat according to this manner until you are well; this is the way of strength.
de la fistule de l’oil	And if you cannot bear all this in that hour, make an ointment from oil and soothing things to soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pain is appeased and the swelling has subsided; then repeat according to this manner until you are well; this is the way of strength.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and medicine with burning water, as I have said before, and it is not completely healed, if there is still something remaining on the incision, leave it in place and drain all the moisture from it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone breaks, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the limb has all the elements to be whole; it is called an "aspre chief," and be made of burnt ivory, that is, a broken bone, and be pointed out as with a lime as when it is in this form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the limb the broken bone, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand until you feel that the corruption is reset; do this never, then restore the limb of exiccative medicines.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is swollen and char is not born, and the bone of the bow is swollen, and remains for eighty days, and does not recover and is not better with treatment, and accidents happen not because of that; know that it is sane; if this is not the case, if there is no other remedy than to restore the fistula to its proper place without delay according to this form: and that is to uncover the bone the second time by iron, and by watery medicines, and when it is uncovered take it out as before according to this form, and make the incision at two angles, and the wound should be narrowed down as much as you see fit:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and move your hand away from the oil.i. immediately, then pull the limb back until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes from under his arm if he keeps his hand on his elbow. de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and move your hand away from the oil immediately, then pull the limb back until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes from under his arm if he keeps his hand on his elbow. Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the limb opens all at once, and there is no displacement of the navel, no swelling, if you must bind the patient; then loosen it, and put on a bandage or dressing in a circular fashion to suck out the wound, then put on oil.i. with acaice and aloe and incense and beeswax, and then strain the oil, and replace it with lint and cloth; and keep the cloth in place if you take cloth enough soft, and double bandage in three layers, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the wound has in it; then strain it by pressing down with a stiff bandage, and reapply the dressing to suck out the wound in a circular fashion; then tie the dressing and leave the oil strained for a night, and if the wound has softened, if you must strain it out; then tie the limb up after the night and the morning, and if you see the oil returning, that is good; if not; continue the dressing and the cloth and the limb and the dressing until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee.

When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, then open the joint, and if there are papers within like grains of resin, leave them; for it is expected to see them. If you see them covered, the work is like biting an awl at the root of the lower part until below the middle, then insert another awl or there is a double thread of the lower part; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl as it lies.
