de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The belly of the oil.
des aigues de l’oil	of the belly of the oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis serre l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, if the water returns to the second opening, place the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly secured and does not rise up, gently remove the instrument from the wound slightly bending the limb. Then pour on the water a little bit of the remaining oil, and wipe off the surplus. Then put on clean oil-soaked bandages or linen cloth with plenty of eggs, and tie with the oil.  Indeed, and those who are of our company, put on a warm compress with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda does not enter the oil because there are too many hairs in the way, since this is the shape of the instrument:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, pierce only the conjunctive [ligament] alone, and do not go too deep, but make a small incision, then insert the lancet, as we have said; and when the work is finished, appears to the patient a yawn that comes from the bowels; and let him lie still, and take light meals, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound according to his disposition until three days; then take him back to the same place where he was before, uncover his eye, and let him see whatever he wishes; then put it back in its place for seven days; and do not let him do anything else until this is finished in the time of treatment or after the incision, but make sure you feed him, for the pain has increased greatly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And thus, after the incision, comes the discharge of oil from the seventh day; take away the oil before the seventh day and give him what relieves the abscess; and when it is calmed, take away the eye and put upon his face a little bandage to cover nothing; and keep him bound in that place. And then go out of the house and back in, and he will recover in his case; and let no disciple interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Yrach region who told us that in their peace they used to do an ointment with honey that when it was applied to the wound, the pain would subside; however, we have never seen or heard of such a thing in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing for us.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for he who does not know them will not recognize them; and be of barley properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their tops are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a goosefoot.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	of the shape of a spearhead from the neck down.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes birth or death does not occur with diverse hairs, for there are some which appear like scorpions at the mouth of the teeth; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with blood of a crimson color, and if there is hair of a sulfurous color. In those in which these hairs are sulfurous, and not entangled, it is enough to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and cover his nose, and spit out the spittle on those hairs, and drive them away; then take what you can hold to support the subtle gut with one hand, until you know that that hair is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has all its instruments lightly held, if nothing is left; and if without you snoring, or incision close to the eye, if the escape is like it should be; and if it is malignant incisions, hasten and cauterize as much as you can until it is stained and the hair is burned over, then spit or do not spit easily, but with pain or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If he does not vomit, and moisture comes up to the throat, saliva that is sane; and if moisture does not come out like it should, saliva that is there is pus in the bones below, behold the instruments do not come out whole: therefore it must be that you drink a thick thread, and keep your hands clasped, and have between each knot no space more or less; and put the patient’s chin on the thread at the front, and treat with odor until it comes through the nose; and many times do the children do this, and it is a light thing for one who has seen it done; then hold the chief that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and take out the one after the other while pressing as we are or with thread. Do this until you are certain that the knot has not corrupted that hair; then draw out the thread, wipe the blood, wet the thread in Egyptian balsam, and put it back in place as before; do this two or three days, until the abscess has corroded all that is left of hair; and then put in or take out a splinter of sponge for some days until it is sane, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the chief, from which we distill oils and medicines or not.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of gold, like a large lamp, if like a sponge; and guide it thus; and if you see, make a close bundle, and make the instruments flat to purge the chief; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when we burn oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the wrist.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the arm a disease which is called “telul,” and it grows and becomes great at once, so that it appears like a thing to behold; and because of this it is expedient that you should commence to apply the cautery or burning medicine at the outset, and break the bone afterwards; and if you delay in covering it when it is great, if you take warning when it is hard, of foul discharge, of bad sense: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a swollen abscess, for when you touch it once, there results great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul discharge, you can see that you can cover it all, if you drain the patient and cover it with oil, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Wounds that occur when a solution of continuation comes into one of these cartillages works, for in some homes. It is therefore necessary that this does not happen to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh at all its borders; then join the two edges of the wound together with a stitch, and cure until it is healed. And if the edges of the wound have already separated from one side and the other, if you must keep all the surrounding parts warm until they bleed, then reassemble the two edges of the wound together with a stitch, and strain, and sprinkle upon it some dragon's blood powder and incense; and put upon the powder a piece of dressing of great or other kind that binds. Leave it until it oozes by itself, then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch is that you reassemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in the costure of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the edges of the wound
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home on the hands there are dense layers of skin, sometimes like grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore it is likely that you will tear the skin and make incisions on each little hair, and grasp them with tweezers and pull them out at the root; then employ the paste after the incision of the little carbuncle, until it is no longer stained; and then remove the paste easily, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the teeth of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times comes upon the gums the white teeth which are called 'albuly'; if you support them, grasp the root and pull out the socket or the blood; then take out the little carbuncle with the vitriole burn or other astringent and drying powders; and if the tooth comes out after the incision, and this happens often, if you grasp it a second time and burn it; if it does not come out after the burn; this is the form of the instruments to cover it
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are gathered at the root of the tooth, within the mouth between the gums, teeth that are white and rough; and never are the teeth black and yellow and soft, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and are the teeth biting; if it is that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulder be in your chest, and open the teeth or the gums open, until there remains nothing; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, as long as they are whole; and if one has what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, if he must repeat the second and third time, until you have done everything; and the teeth that have mixed with various forms of instruments to repair, according to what the work shows, for the raisers of the teeth that you must drive out have other forms than those with which you must drive between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you visible.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you do not leave it too long to treat it as much as you wish, for this must not be done carelessly; for it is a high-quality material so therefore we have no excuse for omitting to drive it out
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to do something, if you are certain that he is capable, many times the pain will depart from the patient. Take care that it is neither too great nor too little; and make him do the bone that he wants to do; and although he does not depart from this pain until the malady has disappeared, as we have already done for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that he is capable, then you must support his tooth firmly for a long time to ward off all harm; then put his thumb and index finger firmly in their place, until they are well secured; and then confirm the fracture well between his thighs, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, when the tooth is placed directly over the break, and if it does not jump out, take no other instruments and hold the tooth loosely from below; and move it as you did before. And if the pulp is perceived and bruised, if you can, fill it with cloth, or if it is perforated, leave it so; and if the fracture is strongly held with pins, do not break it while holding. You must move smoothly over the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first. And take care that you do not do what the ignorant layman do, who break it every time without reason, and do not bring anything but this that we have told you; but bring no bloodshed by the root of this great disease that remains, or by the fracture that they break, as we have often seen; and when the pulp is gone, wash the blood of wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is blood, as it often happens, if you employ the juice of vitriol ground; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, when they are mute at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double much when you draw the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great limbs if they do not bend much when you draw, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so as to hold them in place.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root is loose when you draw, if you must remove the moist cotton swab inside, namely here or there, until the tooth is loosened, and then insert the forceps that are called “algefri,” so that the head of the tooth seems like a beak; and be made as with a file and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument which is called “althali,” which is to say tweezers, for this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and firm, lest it break my skin, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, aid it with all your instruments, for these shapes will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, for this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, whose form is as follows: let this instrument be strong enough not to break, and its handles like those of other instruments for teeth; and there are other instruments which are not mentioned here; and the master surgeon will discover by himself his instrument, according to what his works and his experience show, for there are various diseases for which the old methods do not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it breaks not from bone or other bones, or if it is crooked, if it seeks other instruments, as I have said, and helps with gestures, as is its form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, that it does not slip, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is slight, if the grasp has all of these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not match its natural form, and the shape is unsightly, and even in women of gentle birth, if one should think that it is hidden within the tooth, and is not in its rightful place, and one cannot soothe it or support it: then it must be extracted; and if it is foreign to the tooth, if one grasps this instrument which has this shape, which is like a small beak, and is made of iron without a groove at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And it must be grasped firmly and cautiously with the hands just as long as the tooth lasts, and because of that one must not move the others, and if it appears, it can be limed, if one uses a file like this which has the same shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is just like making nails; and while holding the tooth firmly and cautiously with the hands, if it moves even slightly, if it cries out, the tip should be filed off at the end when it is finished, for if it is too deep it bites the tongue, if one should file away the roughness as much as it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth are loose, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press on what annoys them except by biting, and you must cure them with restrictive medicines, for this is of no avail; if you must restrain them with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and causes pain, but the gums do not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are too close to each other, take the thread and pass it double between the two front teeth, then place the teeth between the front teeth, if there is one or more of them, until you see them clearly up to the neighboring tooth; then resume the covering until you reach the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and clearly, so that it does not move; and if your thread is too long at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then clip the teeth with the thread at some tweezers, and assemble them, and put them back between the neighboring teeth, and put them so that they do not touch the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can remain in place, and if they loosen or the thread breaks, strain with another thread; if it should remain and serve in this way, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the front teeth and the back teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth bites, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and do not let anything interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make its form like that of a chipped tooth, and put it back in its place or the default is there, and strain it as we have said, and remain and serve steadily for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	The tongue is sometimes loosened from its socket or by nature, or by an accident of a deep wound; and the work is such that you must open the mouth of the patient, put your hand on his tongue, and hold it still; then grasp the large nerve of the tongue, as long as the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is any delay or not, and it is a matter of healing a wound, if you touch the surrounding area and grasp the nerve firmly; and keep that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is loosened; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale or cold blood, and put the tongue back in a slight attempt; and bind the patient’s hand, that the tongue cannot move. And if blood comes from the wound, if you pull out the clot; and if it does not go away, if you cauterize with the blunt cautery, which is good for this; then you must cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see pus of a color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining to swell, and there is moisture, if it evacuates the clot, and you make a small incision, and deliver from one side and the other; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a clot and broil it until it is dry, then come back to your work until you have finished all your work; then lift the pale and thick blood, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are often goiter-like swellings in the throat which are called "godath", and which are properly called amandres. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take heed: if they are hard of little size and of a pale colour, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, even though it may cause the loss of blood; but leave them alone until they are dead, and then you may remove them, or they will break by themselves. And if they are of a pale colour and the root is slender, if you have brought the instrument to cover it, look first that the swelling rests and is calmed. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders should be relaxed, and cover his mouth with his hands, and press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, as it is done; and let it be of silver or gold, just like a nail:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, as it is done; and let it be of silver or gold, just like a nail.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form: grasp the one of the nails with one tong, and the other with the other hand; and when you have grasped one nail, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood has drained, if there are still clots of blood, either break them up with pomegranate seeds, or burn them with bay leaves, or similar things, until the wound is clean; then cure as it is healed; and never again shall there be any other incision in the throat except for the two nails, if you grasp them just as the two nails remain intact.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with a small abscess in her throat, which was causing her to be unable to breathe through the passage that was obstructed, and unable to eat or drink, and she died because of this. And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two nails from the two holes that had not been pierced. I then held her hand tightly and put one finger on the abscess and the other on the nail, and when I had grasped the nail I made an incision, gargled the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood had drained, if there were still blood clots, either break them up with pomegranate seeds or burn them with bay leaves, or similar things, until the wound was clean; then I closed the wound and pressed the tongue; after that I put the finger back in the abscess and held one part, and only a little blood escaped from the hole; and when I had finished holding the passage in the throat, the woman was able to drink water and wine, and I continued to examine the abscess for a long time; and the abscess gradually reappeared, filling the cavity that I had evacuated. And I bound and cauterized the abscess within the throat: it went away in a retrograde direction; and I left these parts and only God knows what happened to her after I left.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the limb hangs downwards, and it is loosened and becomes long, if it is called a "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round, if it is called an "uve". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the after-pain has disappeared, and it is subtle, if you must, when you see it, in its color and its length, that you make the patient sit in the sunlight, and press the tongue to the instrument which we mentioned earlier; then close the wound with the needle and thread that we mentioned before. And it must not be closed more than is necessary beyond the natural limit; for if you do, the voice and the tongue will grieve. And after the incision, use what we mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of the closure, it must be used with the cautery from the side of the fear. And the manner of cautery is acute. And it is that the patient puts his head in his hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument which we mentioned or the chapter of cautery, and grasp with live charcoal, if it is not too thick or too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, from which it is known.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the limb hangs downwards, and it is loosened and becomes long, if it is called a "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round, if it is called an "uve". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the after-pain has disappeared, and it is subtle, if you must, when you see it, in its color and its length, that you make the patient sit in the sunlight, and press the tongue to the instrument which we mentioned earlier; then close the wound with the needle and thread that we mentioned before. And it must not be closed more than is necessary beyond the natural limit; for if you do, the voice and the tongue will grieve. And after the incision, use what we mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of the closure, it must be used with the cautery from the side of the fear. And the manner of cautery is acute. And it is that the patient puts his head in his hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument which we mentioned or the chapter of cautery, and grasp with live charcoal, if it is not too thick or too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, from which it is known.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, for the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation as described in this manner, take charcoal and isops and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather all of them together in one pot, and put them in, and boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot put one instrument with a handle as described in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	This cure is safer than incision, for the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation as described in this manner, take charcoal and isops and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather all of them together in one pot, and put them in, and boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot put one instrument with a handle as described in this manner:
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened to me at the throat bone or fish spine, or nothing; so therefore it is right that you should know what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, do make the patient vomit the illness as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach; in case it is expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or some piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to one thread, and then transfix it; and when it comes back, if it is expelled, and then draw it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take one instrument of sponge as described above:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter more easily through the neck, with the head raised up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, for it will not go down, nor will you push the bone inwards; and must you value that the patient has come to take the instrument, for it is either stiff or something is wrong; if the epiglottis is swallowed, or if you force it down with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter more easily through the neck, with the head raised up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, for it will not go down, nor will you push the bone inwards; and must you value that the patient has come to take the instrument, for it is either stiff or something is wrong; if the epiglottis is swallowed, or if you force it down with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And never is medicine good, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look at the patient’s tongue in the sunlight, and when you have pressed the tongue against the instrument that I have told you of. And if you see the tongue, if you force it down with all your might, or if there are tenacles that are worth as much. And if that is not worth it, if you take a toothache, and put it in the patient’s throat, and withdraw or bite the tooth – or burn with the cautery – do that often. And if the patient suffers with great pain, then take a full drink of cold water, and cover the mouth, and swallow, and move the tongue with your hand often; and if you see that with the tongue the patient feels the pain, withdraw it.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not yield as we have said, if you fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will have its effect. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces visible, and let the pot cover be covered with a gauze patch in the middle, and in that hole let the instrument be; then you pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out only through the opening; and the opening will now yield, and if it does not yield, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, eat dirty and foul things, and do not drink water; and thus it will force him that it goes out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is like that which we treat the boils with, if indeed when we see it, it is like a pair of tongs with teeth to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of a heron, and it has a lime-like roughness, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and thus is the shape.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The wounds of the abscess are diverse in their perforation and size; for there are two ways in which they may be classified. The first is when the wound resembles itself, and when it has moisture. The second is when the wound is on the bone or is at the joint. For the wound of the head of the abscess is different from that of the wound of the root, and the wound of the bone of the arm is different from that which is in the joints.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess does not burst by itself, as long as it is painful according to its degree; but if it is of such a kind that it must be burst when it is hardened, and does not die according to its degree, as is the case of abscesses that are drained from joints. For when an abscess is drained from a joint, and it is left in its place, by chance if the tendon and nerve of the joint are ruptured, which is the cause of stiffness in that limb. Or if the abscess is drained from the principal part of the limb, and the perforation is delayed until it is complete, if there is a wound of the principle part; or if it is drained from the root, if the perforation is not complete; you must only pierce the abscess when it is hardened with digestion accompanying, except for the one that is drained from the root, which must be left uninjured, and must be drawn inwards, and there will be fistula; and it cannot heal in a great amount of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	You must cauterize the wound of the abscess when it is painful according to its degree; when the pain is calmed, the swelling has gone down, the fever has gone down, the swelling and redness have gone down, there is no debate or tingling in the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and the place where the pus comes out; and let the perforation be long enough, if the abscess is full of hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all parts that are equal or there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	When the wound bursts open, by the will of the limb itself. And when the abscess is settled, if you leave the perforation open until it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before that, if it has been a while, the poison will spread through it, and there will be plenty of filth; and by chance you will strengthen the wounds and deepen them. And if there is no abscess that is perceived according to the large size of the limb, according to what the limb has suffered. And it is obvious that you must bring in small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that you must chew through to the marrow, cover them; when it is already burst like a drape, and is softened, if you must do the same as with bubbles. And if there are such ones that are split into two angles, and such ones as we cope with the nutmeg, like abscesses of the spleen; and if there are such ones that we make a round size, and others of a similar nature that are coped with.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When there is no head of the sufferer, if there is a superficial abscess, it is obvious that you must pierce it straight through; and when the abscess is large, and it has a great swelling, and you pierce it, if you do not drain all the swelling at that time, but only a part; then stamp the abscess until the other side, and leave nothing more. Do this repeatedly until the swelling is all gone; even if the patient has little strength, or a woman in labor, or a young child, or an old man decrepit. For experience has never shown that there is any success with the discharge of the swelling, except by chance the patient dies, and you will not be blamed for it. Therefore, escape from this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if you wipe the wound, look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is of a moderate size, bring in some lint or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there is plenty of perforation, it is obvious that you must drink in chews one attempt after the other until they meet in the middle; and if you have cut a piece of skin out of the abscess and closed it, if you must, cover it with fine cotton or a sliver of flaxseed soaked in moisture, and leave it for a third of the way; then the bone, and bandage it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are discharges of blood in your work, if you bring in cold and sharp water and soak it for a while, and take out the offending dressing many times. And if the discharge of blood persists, if you bring in government and cure, and the powders that I have said in my hands in this book, and if it is winter and the limb or the abscess is numb, it is obvious that you must put on attempts and soaked cloths with wine and oil; and if it is summer, and the limb is fleshy, it is obvious that you must put on soaked cloths with water and oil, or with wine and oil that has been rubbed, until the third of the way; and then take out the abscess and wipe and bandage it, if it is possible, until it is healed.

de squinance	When the wound is well drained, if the dressing of oil covers the scar, while it is sound.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of the size of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.
