puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess for four days on the needles; if you see them, break the needles and leave the abscess alone until it bursts by itself; kill the pain by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you must pierce it when it is small and soft, then cure it of what is causing it, and leave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is causing it, and bandage the limb.
dou chancre	sore abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have already spoken of the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to shun the cautery. We say that an abscess swells in the marrow, and has great caution in its treatment. The old men say that when an abscess is in the flesh or can be scraped out like an abscess which is in marrow, and in the heel, and in other parts, it must be extirpated as soon as possible; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be brought about, do not approach it, for I know of no cure for it. None of them has ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And in the work, when it is in the flesh or can be extirpated, as we have said, do not purge the black bile from the patient once. Then make the patient well again if there is any visible swelling. Then give the patient a purgative, such as wine, to make the work easier. Then take out the nails or abscesses, and the sinews of all parts, and the bone of all parts round about; and leave the wound to heal naturally. Expect the wound to bleed at the incision of the artery or vein if the cautery is done too much; then cure with another remedy until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already mentioned in the division the signs of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of swelling resemble, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if only the inflammation is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two signs: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore when one administers medicine for this sign which is called "inflammation" by medicine, and the cure brings no benefit, if one observes that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides dropsy, as with all other diseases and like many other things; if one does not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if one sees the patient of great strength, and there is only dropsy besides, and he is neither too young nor too old, then one must work on him.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Hold the patient’s right hand over your hands, and press the abdomen downwards towards the lower part of the belly, then take the thumb and index finger and shape them like this: Make a trench about two fingers wide at the tip, and do not make it so deep that it reaches the intestines when you insert it, and do not bind it.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if dropsy is reaching the intestines: if you think that two fingers’ breadth of fluid has gone into the bowels, make two transverse incisions above the navel; and if the dropsy is caused by liver disease, make the incision on the left side of the belly; and if it is caused by gravel, make it on the right side, and do not make the incision too deep that the fluid runs out of the weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the gut, and hold your hand with all the space between the skin and the bone as when escorting the amount of a nail or an arrowhead; then pierce the bone as far as the space comes to an end, and that is the cause of the pain, then pull out the instrument, and there is left the form of the instrument: and it is similar to a silver awl, and is of steel or an archangel’s wing, and has at the lower part a small hole; or costs two holes, and three on one side, and one on the other; and the nail is cut like a pen, and that is the form of the incision which the writer cuts like a pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the head of this is the ailment, so that when the instruments come to the pain, if you now lift them up from the instruments; drain then half or a third part, for if you drain more than that which can be contained in that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but drain according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue tell the patient, and his pulses; then pull out the instrument and hold back the pain, and it is now retained by the thumb which is pressing the perforation which is on the bone, as I have said, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering from that, and pull out a small amount of pain.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de suivre tant qu’il ne reste plus qu’un peu d’eau. Et si tu douteras sur le patient, et tu y laisse mourir du eau, si le recrute de la sepulture ou du sable chaud, et par mourir de sueur ou de bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boire; et le recrute de médicaments dessicantes tant qu’il soit sain, et cauterise sur l’estomac et sur le foie et sur l’esplen après l’extraction de l’eau, comme j’ai dit précédemment.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do nothing foolish, and keep following until there remains only a little water left. And if you doubt the patient, and you let him drink too much water, if the recruit of the sepulture or the warm sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and take care to drink; and the recruit of drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never is a child born without a hernia in the belly, or the hernia is small, or it is not firm in its place. If you suspect too much that there is no hernia at all, do not attempt to pierce anything. If you wish to do so, take a little piece of lead or plum pudding and bind it and hold it in place for two or three days. And when he wants to urinate, if you keep the closure closed, he will urinate, and then you can release it; and by chance there will be no harm, for the urine that comes out will not leave the closure closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the opening is small, if it is a medicine of lead weight, as we have said, if it expands. Those who have no opening in their limb are black, for none are born with the opening at the head of the bone, for they cannot urinate before raising their thigh; and they cannot evacuate anything because the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and this is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, and the head of the thigh and the hip are as wide as a thumb, if the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and you must take care of the evacuation of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des pustules de la verge	of the thigh
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this white spot appears on the verge, and is a sign of a harmful disease; and in it there are both malignant and benign things. If you take them at their face value [literally "with oil of oncion"], grasp and crush them all, then put on moist cotton in Egyptian fashion; then treat with diafinicon until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the spot is malignant, with colour and discharge, if you must treat it with cautery. When you have grasped it, and if the spot is on the edge of the verge and some is in the hair and some outside, if you must stretch the spot which is inside first; and when it is fractured, if you cure the outside, if you do not firmly secure the edge of the verge that it is not perceived, comes blackening and corruption in the verge or groin; if you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and sometimes, then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if blood comes out, if you must apply the lunar cautery as follows: The cautery should be as follows: at the discharge of blood and at the corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you drink or lead the patient away from the verge a bundle of wool, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has dried out from the head of the verge which have not been circumcised, or there is wound or incision, if you must then burn them with a burning instrument until the limb is loosened, and deliver the limb from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If it is an urgent matter to separate this, if you can, grasp it immediately without causing any harm to the head of the thigh or the heel; then slowly separate between the thumbs, and put a wet linen bandage on it with cold water, so that it does not slip out of place.
de la circoncision	If it is an urgent matter to separate this, if you can, grasp it immediately without causing any harm to the head of the thigh or the heel; then slowly separate between the thumbs, and put a wet linen bandage on it with cold water, so that it does not slip out of place.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely an act of continuing care like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly as possible, if it is necessary that we make it as mild as possible for the patient.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach me circumcision of the children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen that the greatest part of masters and doctors who practiced circumcision did so without knowledge, with force, and with a new instrument; if it happened that the testicles escaped because of two layers of skin, and by chance if one cut through these and left the other behind
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it returns covered, and the pain is doubled, and there is the mutilation which is more than doubtful concerning the tip of the limb; and the mutilation of the bone by chance escapes the wound, and repairs the work, and many times happens that they must undergo mutilation without having had to do so, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made with force throughout the thread I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces tear just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if it is held equally in every way, there is great tension; but if the thread is well twisted around the leather; and if the manner be as at first work, if you make the child think, if he understands, do not make him suffer more than to bind the thread around the limb only as much as is necessary, and then let him go in all the ways that you wish.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then put your hand between your hands straight, and bring the forces between your hands or from your pieces that the child will not see, no instrument; then stretch your hand at the limb and breathe or cough, and pull up as much as the head of the limb is set; then wipe away the dirt that is gathered, then bind the sign with a double thread, then bind from this side to that side as much as is necessary; and hold for two seconds at the pouch and the index finger, and press between the two lines, then release the thumb immediately and pull out the chief of the limb.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood drain freely without restraint, for this is the wisest; and sprinkle powder on and about the wound. i.e. a bandage stuck with a yolk of egg moistened with rose oil and balsam, and leave it on until the bleeding stops.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the limb is deformed in this way: the two bones are tense and bent, and the limb is as thick as a sleeve,
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of deformation is when the marrow is fractured during the incision; therefore it is necessary to stretch your nail so that the wound is open; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold your nail firmly, even if you grasp it tightly, and then cut.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass for two days, and that which is from the root is swollen, if you leave it as long as the spasms subside, and the swelling is slight; if you press it as you can, and hold on to the root, it will avail you nothing.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you press too much over and above measure, and it goes away, it will avail you nothing; cure it as we have said, while it is still sound.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	because of the retention of urine.</start_of_turn>
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from the opilation of a stone, or of blood congealed, or of bile, or of chyle, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the previous division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the stone is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, if it is necessary, you must bend the patient over their knees; place the hand pieces outside the back, and extend the patient's abdomen from the upper part of their back, and restrain the patient so that they do not move as much as possible; and then you must force the neck of the bladder out to the outlet of the stone, so that the urine will flow out immediately.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, if it is necessary, you must administer an extraction with all the instruments which are called "siringues"; for this is the form: either of silver with a slight groove cut, like the beak of a bird; or the caine of a long and a half palm, or something similar to that.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And thus the manner of issuing urine is that you take one double thread and bind one end to a piece of wool or cotton, and pass the end through the syringe; and drain the surplus of wool and pass until you reach the end of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and vinegar of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and the belly with oil moist and olive oil and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the syringe gently into the bladder until it reaches the root of the bladder, and double the bladder downwards towards the buttocks; then drain the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty, for this is not done except in this order save for that which is driven or which goes crooked; then withdraw the thread from all the wool and wool, and the urine follows the thread, and then draw it out, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And resume the syringe until the bladder is empty, and make the patient align.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are urine stones or blood in the bladder, or if it is filled with pus, and you see urine and medicines boiling, if you do everything that is called a «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is pierced at two places: one at the beginning and one at the end, as you see; and you must keep the bladder steady so that the medicine is properly absorbed, if we can drive out the moisture, and evacuate as much as possible is necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see your medicines flowing in the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull out the catheter little by little; if you pull out the moisture at the catheter, and then push it back in strongly; if the moisture enters the catheter, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle blister from which we clip the bladder: if it be thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And this is the form of the subtle blister from which we clip the bladder: if it be thus:
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round; then stretch a strong thread through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned above the methods of handling stones, and their extraction with medicines; and we have spoken of the difference between a stone that is embedded as rain and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened according to its size; and in the bladder, and the kidney; and I shall tell you openly and briefly about them.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder is oftener loose, and this is a sign that it has burst from the bladder as much as from its subtlety; and it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s flank, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then becomes hardened; and from these bursts there is always some sediment; and the foundation is easily loosened for about three years, and is more grievous in the old, and is as common in youths as in old people; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to loosen the patient by clinking, to drive out all the pain that is in the intestines. For it never fails to obstruct the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and it never fails to go down without some movement upwards; then make him sit between your hands apparent, and his hands be placed against his thighs, so that the bladder is totally relaxed downwards; then ask and touch accordingly.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry up now to touch the stone on the stone. And if it does not prick at being touched all around, if you feel more oil from your left hand, if the patient is fat, or from your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; then press on its foundation, and ask for the stone, and when you feel it with your middle finger, if the bladder is full; then press on your middle finger, and the stone will come out either by itself or you will see it spit out.</start_of_turn>
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the hairs above, and with his left hand grasp the skin that is below the hairs in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge with a clap, for thus is its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And place between these hairs and the foundation, do not make them go into the middle but along the left side of the nail; and be upright on the stone, and your two thumbs either downwards or towards the foundation, and take the size through if it is wide by pushing, but inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, do not make it too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if two thumbs are on the stone or the foundation, that it press forward in the work; and the nails that are in the piece or that are angled, and margins: if they are grasped to be stiff; and if there is a piece that is soft, it is like a gland, round, from which there is little issue.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles or margins, make the size larger; and if it does not slip, it is certain that you must draw upon the tenacles which are as sharp as a file at the head, to draw out the stone if it does not escape; or you can give it an emetic, i.e. a mild instrument with a curved handle at the head; if you do not manage to engage it, it is large and will pierce, and if it is without decor, it is like straining with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there are more than one stone, first draw out the largest at the neck of the bladder, then draw up, then push out, and the smaller afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, if you cover it with silk, make a larger wound. For indeed, many things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back towards him more abundantly than it can be bound; but whatever you do, try to drain, or remove the tenacles, until you have drained it piecemeal.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, and hold it together, and put upon it a moist bandage of oil and wine, or of oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his heel and do not loosen the bandage until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it [the dislocated shoulder], if there is much pain in the limb from oil and water, then cure it with dynafinicon oil and balsamic oil until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If pus comes from the wound and corrosion, and swelling of blood in the bladder, or that the urine is retained, which is known in part as without jumping with the urine: then take your dose in the wound, and expel that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away.</start_of_turn>
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound gently and easily and bind it, and help in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and make sure that all the hours you treat it, that you bind the wound tightly and gather the medicines above the limb.</start_of_turn
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	If the stone is small and is either in the bladder or the urethra, and it is fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does what I have said above, then one should listen to the size of this cure. I have already had proof of this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the instrument according to this shape and make it so that there are two angles fixed at the tip: in one hand
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Take hold of the instrument according to this shape and make it so that there are two angles fixed at the tip: in one hand, take a thread and bind it around the base of the stone so that it does not slip back into the bladder; then push the instrument into the bladder lightly until it reaches the stone; and rotate the instrument in the stone back and forth until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the stone is broken and urine comes out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is still in the bladder. If it is broken and spurts out with the urine, and if there is blood, then the patient is sick;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the limb with one hand and with the other grasp the bone above and below, then place your thumb between the two joints, and pull forcefully, loosening the ligament, and move the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure as long as it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the limb with one hand and with the other grasp the bone above and below, then place your thumb between the two joints, and pull forcefully, loosening the ligament, and move the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure as long as it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is dislocated in women, and this happens only once, it is a serious ailment which is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that no woman knows who has seen her uncover herself as much as she does, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman who knows this art of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman's stone is more prominent than the man's, for in that case it is possible to make a deeper incision, and there is greater fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If necessary, if you take a mistress who is well aware of this, and prick her flesh, and if you do not find her, know that she is a cunning woman; and present her with a gift that is worthy of a woman of sense, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command of her with inquiry of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look well if the woman is a virgin: then you must push forward her breast or foundation and inquire about the stone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her breast, command her to hold her breast or with the patient, and want and press her left hand on the bladder nearby
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If this be true, then command her to move from the groin to the knee of the limb entering the bladder as far as she can reach the root of the thigh; then place your thumb on the knee at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone which is usually hidden, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move your thumb above the knee or below, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then hold the limb steady in the size, if you feel the bone so twisted that the wound becomes larger than it should be, and that many times bones have been fractured in this way: for small, large, rough, smooth, long, and round bones have all been known to fracture. If the fractures resemble each other, it is clear that the bone has been dislocated.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not mend, if you put on a coarse plaster and hold it for an hour until it is dry; then return to your work, until the bone is healed, and have the instruments that I have mentioned for extracting the bone as your home will aid you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go by itself, and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and strain with sponges and bandage, and do not resume this treatment any more; leave the wound alone and do not touch it, except in the case of an accident that causes the patient’s death; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of blood is calmed and the limb is relaxed, if you return to this work while the wound is still open.
de hernie carnouse	from a herniated abscess
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white wax, which is as soft as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "wax," and never is it properly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that it is not otherwise. And it is the skin of the seed between the white wax that we have said. That does not happen by chance.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramus is weak and comes from the seeds, and that matter is spread out
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it happen that it comes from percussion on the seeds, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or pale blue, and so on
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of a dislocation of this assembly, for if it is white or pale as we have said, if the abscess is prolonged, that is to say as long as the figure of a fist, and does not yield to pressure, because there is moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is prolonged with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that it is another fist;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the coions and the white surface, if you feel it well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it is like that which is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, which follows the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if it be known that the patient is safe according to this, then we anoint him on his back, on something rather high, and put drops of oil on his cloth;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the limb to the loin of the ribs like two nails of a nailboard
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the sponge, and grasp the skin of the ribs among the ribs from the loin to below the navel, and make a complete incision straight across the skin of the ribs until the white marrow is seen, and evacuate it carefully as much as possible.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the cavity plain with water, that is to say, a large opening, and drain all the water, and then put on your gloves, and extend the cavity upwards; and do not touch the root of the ribs, but only the cavity itself; cut straight or in pieces immediately the cost of him secretly, for if you do not cut it well it will return the water.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the urine spurts out from your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work of the cavity; then reassemble the two bones of the ribs to their natural position, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the urine corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut off the limb at the whole suspension, drain the urine, and cure it like we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the swelling is collected in three parts together, their roots which are two in number; if one part is cut like the first one equally, then wipe the blood away and put on the wound a layer of soft linen soaked in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	put on another layer of soft wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two joints, and put under doubled cloths, and tie it up in such a way as is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool like this form and assemble them by sewing in the armpit, and one of the arms should grasp from the foundation to the back, and the other from the armpit to the side; and the other two fingers grasp the two angles, and be all assembled together the restraint in the armpit loop
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this caustic twig of cautery sufficient in size like iron; take rather a cautery of the pointed kind, and grasp the hair of the beard, and if it is split as we have said, if the white substance which contains the venom is revealed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery in this fashion, and prick that abscess as we have said, and burn with this subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And grasp in every way that you wish, until you have burnt through it; and keep that fire away from the urine; and soak that thing that has been burned is more salve; and keep away from discharge of blood, and more painful than the work of size;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	If nothing else hinders you, or if you are forced to make an incision or evacuate blood, or any other thing, do what hinders you, following the instructions given beforehand.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	If the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this work due to its horror, if he suspects perforation, as I have said, and you are well certain by the signs that the watery swelling has subsided,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then seat the patient down on a level surface; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with all the surrounding tissue wide open, and make the perforation deep enough so that all the pus can drain out; and if the hole is large, so that all the pain is relieved
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the limb and bind it, and leave only the remaining fluid to drain; then cure until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white wool does not allow the fluid to drain from the wound, if you are to drink a penny or the instrument used to treat the hydrops, as is the custom; then enlarge the wound, and let the fluid return, and reassemble after twenty days or when convenient, and when reassembled as before, the patient will then be cured.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Wounds which in this section of the twig have fear in more than one place, for it seems to me that the pain is worth leaving them alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I shall tell you about the work and the signs of the incision
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that main and forearm come or swell, and sometimes there are coions; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known by excessive rubbing and striking, which is spread with coions, or percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the color of an abscess like the color of honey; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess that swells.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes it is an abscess that is painful and bloody, with a foul color, and never comes from a vein, or from an inflamed vein.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the position of the abscess from the heat of the cautery, when you press it to your chest;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	you must not touch it.</start_of_turn
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made of swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain in the toes.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the size above this semblance, and above the other parts;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you grasp the testicles like worms, then the egg is high, and the thread from the testicles is white silk, and deliver the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soaked with these threads, if it is to be known, that you must then treat the egg and hold it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is exposed to air on the surface, or within the vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage comes loose from the bone or remains behind, if you must grasp it all, and pull out the root, as we have said
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you apply a dressing of coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then bandage the wound until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the incision of the hip bones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling a berry, with softening of the bones.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain when he moves it.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and this disease is very painful like the one mentioned above,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	we will tell you about this matter, according to what the elders have said.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit in a comfortable position, on an elevation, and then suspend the support of the collar around his neck from your two hands.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	At the same time as you bring forward the vessels that arise from the edge, and grasp them with your master hand, and extend them forth;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then clamp to the cutting spatula wide through which the vessels are traversed, until they are uncovered,
