puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or if there is double thread, I bind it to the first root or the head of the nail has come, and I bind it to the other root;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I compress the swelling in the middle directly, according to the length of the bone, and I drain the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I cure the wound if like the others or I bandage it, so that no vessel is damaged that would bleed the contents of the wound;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for in this way there is no harm, and if all the vessels come to the head, if you must, you must drain the wound from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is of extension downward of the scapula, if there are many and many, in long tension, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the scapulae are equal until the margin, because the scapula presses the intestines.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the scapula is sectioned, that it immediately causes pain at the shoulder, and the scapulae are different in position, from the edge to the skin, because of the displacement of the intestines and the hardness of the scapula.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does the bone move with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cures with fear, for fear of them, it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of this work is that if you command or patient that he embrace his intestine with his hand at the bottom of the wound, if he can return it
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either hold his collar between your hands, and keep the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the arm at the shoulder, and close all the skin of the flanks from end to end;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then from the depth of the wound, as much as its size allows, according to what you must do to open the wound, and whatever is necessary; do it in such a way that it does not burst.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then pull out the fat that is below the skin, as much as the blunt part of the wound is uncovered; leave the fatty tissue uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then insert your two fingers into that which supports the bone, between the white tissue that is under the outer skin and between the second tissue,
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and pull out that which is behind the bone, and between the second tissue; and with the right hand grasp the bone of the bones, and extend the white tissue upwards with your left hand, and hold the bone to the whole of the tissue towards the size.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And instruct the minister to extend the arm upwards, and loosen that which is above the bandage.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And look if there is any intestine or white fat wrapped around the bone, and if you find nothing, if the belly swells;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or if there is one, thick thread made of twenty threads, and pass it through the back part of the fat, which is behind the skin of the buttocks; after that the size, and then cut the hair that appears from the threads, until there are three threads left;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then gather them together one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the fat, which we have said is behind the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of three parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then cover the head of the shoulder with folds of cloth, and bind them firmly in three places, so that no vessel other than those which nourish it can enter there, except for incisions.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And straighten the limb according to the first limb that is long three fingers from this one, and after these three fingers leave space sufficient for the socket which is as broad as two thumbs;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	And afterwards all the rest according to the curve which the ear carries; then press in the part which is as broad as the leather of the nails, as much as it does not strain, and bend, as we said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then mix flaxseed with oil, and apply it to the wound, and bind it up as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never burn the fat surrounding the wound as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the limb as long as it bleeds through; and if it swells too much, if it is raised with warm water, and put on what we have said, until it stops bleeding
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound of another way, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this limb I never saw anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old folks say that it is made just like the limb that joins the vis, in part like tying up blood vessels, after the size above lightly towards the outside;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cover it in the middle, and cure the abscess of what causes it, until the blood vessels are quiet; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never comes routine with pain, as we have said, and open the eyes; and do not feel any intestines as companions, and if any are present, it is enough, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and if they stay too long in this place, if you believe the wound or swelling, as long as the intestines are present;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the stretching of the sinews which are in pain, as we have said, because they are stretched, then become softened and relaxed the eyes open.</start_of_turn>
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is in the cautery, as we have mentioned before; and never by fire in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies comfortably upon his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the routure enfleit downward as much as necessary according to the quantity of two fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then draw out the scab which is beside the skin that covers it, then take hold of the root and bring out the limb appearing from the scab.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press toward the belly, then cut the two fingers that appear from the scab on the head of the root, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then draw out the root, and do not cover the scab or extend the gut or anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then he treats the wound. And when you have completed the stitches, if the wound leaks and heals the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scab is constrained, and has no appearance in the course of treatment, and the burn is mute in this limb, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in households, because the bones that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie down on his back, and to scrape off the softened skin from the natural skin; then assemble the layers of skin with a bandage, and if you see it, close the first excess of softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then scrape between the stitches, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The burns caused by the cautery are usually despised in our laws; however, for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to do so except for two methods: one is that the owner of the burn responds when asked, and the other is that we often have to cauterize certain animals for our assistants, as with a goat or a sheep or a cat and other animals. I say therefore that cautery is performed in two ways: by traction or by incision. In the traction method, we seat the best in warm water, until the boils are softened and for a while; then we grasp them with our hand until they are set and we no longer feel them. As for the cautery of great size: it is necessary to hold the best and press the skin of the boils with our left hand; then bind the dressing and apply pressure to each wound with one hand, when they are well secured; and leave no trace of blood or any trace of blood vessel that is outside the blood vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction remains by chance no trace of the boils, because the best desires to loosen. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermofrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres: une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphrodism is in accordance with two methods: one if between the two testes opens just like the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in their urine. And the other method if it is in women, and has on the navel just like a boy and two testes. And the cure of the tumor and envy if it is that you remove all the testicles, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second method, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testes, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a tumor that is above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it just like a hand, and this is the cure. It is necessary that you hold the excess of the tenticle at your hand or as an ointment, and treat it lightly; and do not be too rough, for blood does not live there, and the cure is like any other cure as long as it is healthy; and there is another thing that comes out like a bag of barley, and for this reason it is called the old "madness of the mare". If you can cure it, as we have said the tenticle, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	If the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or if the rupture is small; it is natural by birth, or by accident from disease that comes with it; or it is caused by a sudden movement of the jaw, or a swelling of the face or of the eyes, and is made by pushing in the belly, or on the sides, or on the genitals, or whatever; and the conception, and the birth, and by chance the flowers must have. And the knowledge of this is by the regard of the dance. If the swelling appears close to the two breasts, if you are in a hurry, and the woman is behind you, spread out her legs; then the two breasts will form, as long as the swelling of the face is round, and over the swelling. Then take hold, and mix oil, and put it on the wound, and put the woman at home chest to chest, if it cannot be closed. And if the swelling is hard and thick, it is advisable that you leave it to the sponge resembling a bay leaf. If the swelling is of the jaw, if you suspend it at the navel and leave it; have medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with many eggs; then give a large dose of ointment, so that the wound cannot close. And let it be long, and give a try of dry lint; then it will be cured of other cures until it is healed. And if there is a swelling of the jaw in the belly, if you cover it according to this method, it will not be an abscess. For an abscess is not an eruption of pus in the belly.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emoroids are open veins that without support are usually not accustomed; and when old become tough. And we have said previously concerning the signs and symptoms, and I shall say those which remain to cure. I say that emoroids and tough skin, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except with the cure by iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the needle steady, grasp its root, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw the pieces an hour later, then put them into cold water; and if it bleeds, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and yeast, and make one application upon her back. And if it clots, that is good. If not, if it is bleeding profusely, put on a bandage at the back and has large wounds; then take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine old, and make it bleed. And when the incision is healed, if the wound is oily until it is healed; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the tough skin; and then it is healed until it is healed.

And the after-effects of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emoroids are open veins which without support are usually not accustomed; and when old become tough. And we have said previously concerning the signs and symptoms, and I shall say those which remain to cure. I say that emoroids and tough skin, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except with the cure by iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the needle steady, grasp its root, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw the pieces an hour later, then put them into cold water; and if it bleeds, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and yeast, and make one application upon her back. And if it clots, that is good. And the after-effects of the marrow are many, such as chancre, pierced abscess, herpes, piles, fistulas, emoroids, and chapped abscesses, and other diseases that I mentioned in the division. It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatment the chapped abscesses that come in the marrow, which are not simply abscesses that are closed together; and if you want to know the progress of the treatment, look at the color of the abscess at the beginning and at the end of treatment. Do not be in a hurry to open the abscess, but keep it closed with a cloth bandage or silk stocking. And when the abscess is drained, if you cover the root of the abscess, at the level of the jaw or the spleen, do not remove the dressing until the bleeding has stopped. And when the abscess is healed, if it is oily until it is healed, do not remove the dressing, but leave it in place for a few days. And when the wound is healed, put a few stitches of silk or cotton thread around the edges of the wound and a layer of gauze or cotton wool over the wound and the surrounding area.
de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. The midwife first learns what is the natural posture of an infant, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down on the navel and desirous of smelling the afterbirth: then the child is born immediately; and when the infant’s feet are born according to the natural figure, and the head is delivered first, and is supported by her; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on the abdomen, so that the child is thrust out; for when he descends on his head, if he is supported by her, and is delivered headfirst, it is because his limbs and hands have been delivered by violent delivery; and this is not natural. For it never comes except by force of the womb or the head, or the arms, or that it comes on the abdomen or afterwards, and is changed by an accident from his collar, and by other harmful figures; if the midwife is skilled in the art and has learned well in these matters, and is wary of errors and deceptions, and I will show her all the figures that she must use to aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child is born naturally through the birth canal, and the woman gives birth, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and as soon as she has relaxed her oil or vernix caseosa, then put her in the water between her two thighs where it is formed:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment. puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then grasp it at the joint of the limb or the root, and so it must be that you do the same with the other hand, and make two thumbs.</start_of_turn>
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	and if the limb of the child is big and it is twisted in coming out, or if it has or chief pain assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is certain that you have displaced the spinous process between your two vertebrae, and you make the head and stretch the area, then draw out the pain.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	Or you can rotate it with the instrument which is called the "almidach", from which it comes with the instruments or the chapter that follows this one.</start_of_turn>
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in this way make it swell with a great natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat for the bones as tenacious,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the shoulder joint suddenly dislocates and is forced, if it is fractured, while the moisture that is either there or comes out is still there;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be reduced, if the bone snaps into pieces with the movement that you make.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is embedded in the belly or if the ribs are fractured, if you must pierce through as much as the moisture corrects.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on its side, if the limb is attracted downwards, and the approach to the mouth of the wound is easier.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or the wrist, it is suitable that you extract it [the swelling] with a drape wrapped around the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and keep the belly or the wrist, as long as the moisture which is in it is corrected
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if another limb is fractured, and the limb is dislocated,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	if the limb is struck by a stone or something heavy, and the limb is treated up to the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then indeed, one must anoint or grease it, and do the treatment.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if there is moisture in the wound, it is held back by the cautery which has been done, if one cannot bear to travel,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then one must bring moist and oily things along.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and one must apply poultices, and soak in soft water that is moistening and soothing.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	If the forearm is resting on its costal margin, and you must set it even, if necessary remind what was said concerning the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If he does not recover, if his limb is torn away piece by piece, and you leave nothing of the second limb behind.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if what we have said concerning abscesses comes to pass as often happens in the marshes.</start_of_turn
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if blood comes out, whether from a restricted vein or other cure.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom a fetus had died, then consulted another concerning it, and refuted the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the belly, and it grew so large that it burst, and began to cause great pain.</start_of_turn>
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to seek help, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong dressing, and out came a bone, and after that some days another.</start_of_turn
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at you, for your belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I wish for the wound to be healed, and with hands of bone, as long as the woman is in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and saw the woman long tense and thus bowed down with her head;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have never seen this chapter except for the time when the master found an unusual thing that he had to help with.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, which we call books; and at this time there are two tears of blood from two veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the corners are more subtle of restriction, and are made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth be full of soft things, such as dates and almonds, and of long duration, a palm and a half in length.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And let the two lips be supported by these same soft things, which are closed in one and the other, half a palm or more in length.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two supports are put in the mouth of the patient to open when the two corners are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of the teeth;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And thus are there again six joints in the arm, as you see, from the elbow to the wrist, two of large size.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you see the arm open with all its instruments, if you make the woman sit with her head low, the pieces nearby and the legs extended,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then grasp the two joints together in the arm, and hold the chief of the instrument between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand over all the instruments, as if you had made the handle equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the arm, until it makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very burdensome, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one sees them appear, the work hastens, and the houses are more numerous than before.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not despair of the instrument that has not appeared, for its need is not to be excused.</start_of_turn>
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second [tooth] is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to retain its socket, and then make her spit it out with force, and restrain your hands to the mouth and the chin.</start_of_turn
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it leaps out for this reason, well and good.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot and make a hole or incision, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the mare, like chamomile, rue, anis, camomille, cassia and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, whether cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a leech or incision in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and keep the hair inside the mare until the steam comes out of the mare; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second limb is affected by the disease.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not better, as is commanded in the dance, let her wet her left hand in oil of sesam or in alum, and then put it back in its place.</start_of_turn>
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and if the second limb is affected; and when she has found it, if she grasps it and extends it forward and backward, so that the marrow does not bleed at the extraction.</start_of_turn
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move gently to and fro, and then treat; for if it comes and dries, it will go away.</start_of_turn
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is fractured, as we have said, for the cure we have mentioned, and fumigation of herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that we have said, if you keep silent;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marrow, you bind to the hip of the woman, and then close with oil tetrafarmaçon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she cries and is reset, and comes out forcefully; but nevertheless, when she has cried if there comes a bad odor to the stomach and the head, and bleaches the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, indeed, to perform fumigations, take heed: neither of the ancients has ever experienced fumigation with rue herbs and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the time of her menses and of the second stage is thus: ...
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	It is like a cane, and one puts the upper part over the fire, and the hair above the fire; ...
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	Or on can do fumigations over charcoal, and the pitch until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	When a limb is born without properly perceiving its foundation, it is stamped upon by something subtle which hinders its growth.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	if you wish to cause it to pierce that obstacle at its root, and do not pierce it too deeply, and keep the surrounding area untouched
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on soft padding made of wine and oil, and then the dressing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will stay in place, if you put or pull out a splinter of lead, leave the hands still for a while, and keep the limb still as long as the patient sees the fever rise in bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never comes this time from the stamping of wounds or incisions; if you must cover that stamping: if it be cured, as we have said of the splinter of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	are nodules and grow larger as they come from below the foundation, or from between the two parts of the body,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or several; and when that swelling is old, if it is on the back, and is accompanied by moisture that oozes white or pale blood,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	If there is a fistula or several; and when that swelling is old, if it is on the back, and is accompanied by moisture that oozes white or pale blood, they never disappear; and they are known by the fact that the patient evacuates or expels material through them, or by the fact that there is an opening or wound in the neighbourhood of the fistula when the patient evacuates.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate as far as the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach as far as the joint of the hip, and even to the coccyx bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus it is known that the fistula persists at the foundation, and does not disappear:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus it is known that the fistula persists at the foundation, and does not disappear: and that you bite your thumb or foundation, and there comes out a fine needle of spider or iron in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, if there is a attempt of a sponge, or hair, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair on your thumb;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of blood, no pain, no wind or fever, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	The wounds that they do not pierce through; if you hurry to cure them.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is made through to the bladder or the urine tube, if in a leap the urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is made through to the hip joint, if there is a vein running up to the root;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no swelling and pain in the joint, if it is only slightly bowed, and no medicine or remedy with oil is of any use.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these fistula people have no other cure but toil, and the vanity of empty minds that intervene between them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	And that which is neither new nor ancient, has hope of health through iron, as I have shown
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and lies between your hands on its back; and the legs are stretched out to its hips, and the hips are inclined towards the belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then there is an attempt of an spider, or a plunge if there is discomfort, until you feel pain or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels the pain at the root, if you must drink your thumb and index finger,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	If the patient feels the pain at the root, if you must drink your thumb and index finger, you must know that he has already perceived it; and either uncover the root or if you feel between your thumb and index finger the marrow or bone, then there is swelling that is persistent.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you do not uncover it immediately, it will not heal.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We can do nothing to cure it well without uncovering it; there is indeed some;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the aid which is done with it [the fire cautery] is that if it is grasped firmly the cautery is done according to the size of the fistula, as it is said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And the rest is burnt in the fistula, as far as it comes from the root; do this once or twice, until you are sure that these hairs must be burnt, which are like a bundle of hair
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of moist wounds is made with blunt needles, as long as the hair has not burst, and then the cure of ointment is made with oil and solder.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is well, that is good. But if not, it cannot be cured;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if it [the head of the shoulder] attempts to slip in, do not force it past the root which is either the bone or the foundation; and between the root and the attempt, cover with a thick covering of hair or silk, and you will see the fistula at that which sustains the covering from breaking.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the root of the fistula has slipped forward before the attempt, and the burn afterward, until it reaches the top of the attempt;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be freed from the attempt, and will recover; then smear those hairs which seem like a sparrow’s feather, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he will not move, and if there is a wound between you and the work, if the fire cautery or medical potion is rough.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery joins together two bones: that is to say, the burning of these bones around the edges, the effusion of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the treatment of wounds full of pus, in burn or in cut, until the bones burn in the wound;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound of the suppurating wound with dry herbs, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the thumb or root of the bone is grasped or pulled out, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the attempt, and between these is the thread or silk or cord, or it is close to piercing, if there is no greater force than the way of escape and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you bind it until it is healed, or if you wish you may do so with attempts and care as before.</start_of_turn>
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not be too hasty, for you must cover the support that holds the foundation, and let the egestion go in the natural order.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	Then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it is well, or you loosen the covering and the wound is again covered after it has been cut from the foundation, or by means of a hook or other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then bind up this wound which is in the wound, as you are able;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula at the lower part of the foundation: if it is a less serious matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And never are fistulas cured in this way: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either too late or costs the undermining of the lower part of the foundation under the skin.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perceived attempt at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you see that the thread is torn in two, and the attempt is at the root of the fistula until it is at the head
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If the limb hangs low at the root of the bone, then grasp the thread of that limb which hangs down, so that you swallow the root or the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	If you pull the head of the limb and reunite the joints together, and strain one against the other, and leave it hanging one or two fingers;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it never, until these hairs that are between the bones and nails are cut off.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to burst in every way you can, it will not be too deeply seated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suffice to make the opening wide by force, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is sound
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the thorny spawl from which the fistula arises is rough and trenchant;

ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or when it boils and pricks and stings,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And the intestine was forced out as much as the belly was bony;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	nevertheless did this wine restrict it, and was mute that awe soul because of swelling
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, if moist urine of the intestine is full or high and cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this means is the entrance to all things aligned;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	If it cannot enter, if you make a hole in the wound with the instrument, grasp the blood clots;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to dry the wound that is the size.</start_of_turn>
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	it should not be cut excessively without great necessity.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If the limb hangs limp and rigid in the armpit, and cannot be pulled out, and if this be its form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is swollen and the intestines protrude,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is reset according to its natural form in its own place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	but if you do not, for it is worth nothing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	if you think that you can manage the patient on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	put their legs higher than their head;

et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	If the head and the arm are higher than the lower parts, and the shoulder joint is dislocated in one of the two parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then put the upper part of the limb higher than the lower part;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus you must consider the wound to be great and deep.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds cause that which appears to you.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then hold between your hands, that is to say, place your hands under it, so that it holds all the way along its course.
et assemble les levres;	and close the jaws;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	that is the common method of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	And take an awl or more, according to the quantity of the wound's size.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then leave the head of the wound, that is to say give it some space, and pierce with an awl or if there is need, a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the skin with the awl or needle through the fat and muscle,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	so that it is detached from the skin to that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	And gather the joint of the shoulder with the three joints together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain a double thread around the hook of three parts.</start_of_turn>
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and assemble the three heads of the wound together immediately,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one space and insert another hook;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then the thread will follow as if you had made the first hook.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you have made as many hooks as you desired

et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the hooks are softened, between soft and hard,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	For the subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and the too large ones if they do not penetrate me well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is necessary that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	neither must they pierce too deeply the fat and the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they must not break or open the wound before it has healed.

et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the head of the needles to hold them in place,

et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For there is often a thorn or something sharp.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second costure is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and is that you assemble the shoulder bones together with the cartilages and the fatty tissue, with a thorn or if there is much thick thread in between;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	for the fire of the cautery is hot and makes the fat move.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you leave it at the start or if you have begun it, in this manner we shall tear out the nails.

ceste costure sevent li home,	this rib is for the body,

qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	Who was the master of a knife,

et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The wound was closed after .xv. days, and the cure was applied, and it healed well.</start_of_turn>
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they said of the miracle that it had saved his life, and this was a miracle.</start_of_turn
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not fear death, for I was in a place where there was neither medicine nor any remedy;

Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or thus I will tell you of the three proper methods of dressing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pass it under the lower part until it reaches this depth;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right angle of the right, if you see that the chief is swollen or cramped or that you have pulled the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And the pain comes from another side from the inside until it escapes;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And the understanding of this condition is that if you touch as the leatherworker does the leather,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and once you have let go of one side of the scab, and grasp it from the other side, until the condition is fully remedied.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of treatment is that of Galiens, which is done promptly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If it is thus as if no one does it, who assemble the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and touch one head to the other head, in a straight line.

et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	then leave the two parts joined together;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then draw the needle and make it pierce from the lower part up to this very point,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	Then draw the needle and make it pierce from the lower part up to this very point, as is often done with fractures of the scapula.</start_of_turn>
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then draw the needle and make it pierce from the lower part up to this very point, in other words, through other bones that are opposite each other.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the common way of treating and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	If anyone doubts this word, and no one bears witness,

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The wound is judged to be as painful as others like it:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved,

et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And the limb moved once again when it was supposed to be healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other remedy in these situations except for simple wounds.</start_of_turn>

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	When the chief is burned in the intestines, and there is no further discomfort to the patient,

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Wounds and incisions, when they burst, if they are called universally "fistules",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and indeed when they are split and the wound has burst.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	it is indeed called a fistula when the wound is tough and bloody, or when there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	it is as if the pen of a bird were broken;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And never in a clear bow, and sometimes loosely;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	And never in a clear stance, and sometimes loosely; sometimes almost, and sometimes rather.</start_of_turn>

ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is only by one of the eight causes:

car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from great veins, and from arteries, and from nerves.

car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the liquid bursts through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture is so thin from one hole to another, and fills the world;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then when the wound is clean and your hand is still, if you know whether there are bones or nerves, and if it is firmly closed,
