et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	Then it is necessary to hold the abscess steady and tight until it reaches the root of the tooth; and by chance it will heal entirely
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corruption up to the bone, causing great pain; and the limb becomes pale and swollen.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you have treated it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If it is certain that you have copied it there, do all that is superfluous that is remaining from the limb.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.</start_of_turn>
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very useful when the bone is sound, and the limb is painless;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and the nail approaches the marrow, and begins to prick, and the blood flows,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	If you suspect that I have set the bone wrongly, do not move the limb further.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and grasp firmly but gently the limb above and below.</start_of_turn>
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on the remainder of the limb medicines that are warming and corrosive to dry out all.</start_of_turn
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bandage the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, if the head of the bone is fractured, and the marrow is forced out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the bone fractured, if the head of the bone is broken as it is said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then you must cure it as long as it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and bloody, and if it causes great pain, if you must make it well first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then take the hook of the sponge and cut across from below.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And guard that the cut does not reach up to the area below the hook, because the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is bleeding, put something above which will soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be great.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Two joints that arise in the hands of certain people by chance are always fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is a part where there is bone, and never a nail.</start_of_turn>
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us two must do.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	he who is born in no way must not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And thus, that which is born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance changes its place.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	its size being slight, in part only visible:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	its root is covered by a wide fold of skin.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is grief to cure: if you hold it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In him who is born or must afterwards not, if it be known that you must first cover the round bone until the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it be known that you must cover the round bone until the bone is formed, then cover the bone to a suitable extent at first, and then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come about must be reassembled either by birth, or by healing of a wound, or by fire cautery, or by like things.</start_of_turn
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it be known that you must cover the round bone until the bone is formed, then cover the bone to a suitable extent at first, and then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two bands or cloths soaked in rose oil, which do not stick to each other.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of soft lead, as long as they adhere, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When they adhere to neither side with the palm, if they adhere too tightly.</start_of_turn
Des vils	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large veins enclosed with fatty matter filled with black bile, which comes with many members of dark colour.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often in those who walk and work and carry burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not administer any purgatives of col, and then the remainder of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	Iron is cured in two ways: one with vinegar, and the other by burning the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And thus if you tie up the vein and pull it out forcefully.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	Then if you bind up the vein and pull it out forcefully. The size of this method is as follows: first pull out the hot water bag forcefully, until the bulge is no longer discernible,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the limb of the patient from under the armpit down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then hold the vein in one, two, or three loops, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then believe and command the black blood out of your hand, from the thumb to the little finger, as many times as the patient can endure; for as much as he can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then hold it [the hand] firm, and command him to grasp a piece of meat with his black nail;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and comfort the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The nourishment of the limb is as follows: open the patient’s limb, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then he puts in the poultice or bath, and the limb becomes warm and red, and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If there is no bath available, if he heats the area with fire, and then holds it over the vein for a long time at the shoulder or in the lower part at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then he should cover the skin with fat, and massage the vein carefully from the chest downwards, until it swells up when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you will see it red and black, and when it comes out, the skin looks like a pale thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then stretch the limb upwards, until it is freed from the skin, and then insert the thumb gently.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then stretch the limb upwards, until it is freed from the skin, and then insert the thumb gently. Then support the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then stretch the limb upwards, until it is freed from the skin, and then insert the thumb gently. Then support the limb at the root, as you have done before, and insert the thumb at another place, as you have done before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then stretch the limb upwards, until it is freed from the skin, and then insert the thumb gently. Then support the limb at the root, or several if necessary, and then insert the thumb at the end,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then the trace and keep juice up to the second size; then draw out size by size, until it is all gone, then finish.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not pull it out and lift it, if there is a strong double thread at all its ends,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	tie and pull, and there will be blood at the root, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep that it does not swell, for if it swells, if we cannot pull or lift it, there will be harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have finished treating it, if you take out the foreign body from the wound, soak the limb in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	When the limb is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	So you must grasp it firmly but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron from which the shoulder is made is curved, and do not cut through it, but only grasp the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of great concern, for if it were subtle, it would close the vein; but let it be large as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes in another place except in the limb, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decomposition that comes from the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If it comes from within the body serpent-like and towards, grasp between leather and bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	If there is a sign of swelling in this vein if there comes into the limb a great swelling,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it will swell and the vein will burst like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the limb opens, if you must cover it that you wrap around one third of its circumference with cloth, up to three fingers’ breadth, and the nail,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and leave the scab on the limb, and every time it points towards the heel, if the surrounding tissue covers the scab, and the new growth.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns inwards, and causes swelling and inflammation or pain, and disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of that it must be treated throughout and throughout until it is completely healed, and nothing remains or remains stiff.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de cinq paumes de longueur, ou de dix.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and never is this vein when treated with five fists of length, or ten.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	when it is full; and either empty its contents or bring medicines inside so that there is no swelling, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	and never is this vein like hands wide open, and even when it opens in the armpit, or at the elbow,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes out from the wound, and as soon as it leaps up; cure it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And it comes out from the wound, and as soon as it leaps up; cure it then as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	And it comes out from the wound, and as soon as it leaps up; cure it then as we have said before
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And it comes out from the wound, and as soon as it leaps up; cure it then as we have said before.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And he feels very well aware of every limb, as soon as he feels the skin or it moves, and leaps up fiercely.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And he is plagued by the swelling of humors, as when they approach and become serpents and worms and lice or belly-ache;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and he doubts his malice, for when he goes through the chest and climbs to the head, and comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	then it returns by chance, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if it cannot be forced until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	if so, then you must tie up the limb firmly and support it with a strong thread that is tightly bound.</start_of_turn>
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then pull up and treat it, and if it is pierced by the bone, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then burn it with fire until it dies.</start_of_turn
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it makes is when it contaminates the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or near the oil, immediately grasp its bristles and hold it down firmly.</start_of_turn>
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and must provide the patient with nourishment of various medicines to expel the harmful humors from the body.</start_of_turn>
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and must abstain from eating rotten meat.</start_of_turn
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind-swelling
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and is a pain that comes in the joints of the limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and thus it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and saw her arm swollen, and found a small swelling in the armpit of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And thus afterwards, the vises mount like a worm at the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more tense than anything else, like living silver when it breaks from its root
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that root and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards corrected throughout the limb, until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back towards the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered what he meant by that, because I had never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I must say that I do not know what to do in such a case, when pain in one limb is transferred to another
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not know it myself, as I have seen it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought that it was for this reason that the woman had dry skin and exposed veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason appeared that cold wind was restrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear to me in accordance with this reason for those who are fond of them, and who have moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	When you see the cure for this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the limb above and below is affected, and then supports above as this wind opposes the limb, it is necessary.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	then burn the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the limb is relieved of these winds, like foul pills, and slippery pills, and other similar things.
Des saiettes	From patches.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are varied, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they cause.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are various towels, some with large points, some with small points, some with bristles, and some with buttons.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	some with corners, and some with long handles, and some with fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	or in the great limb it is pricked; ou en membre de dessous qui est plus proche du corps.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	If the brain, head, liver, heart, arm, hand, intestine, bladder, and other members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When one suspects in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must know that you must avoid the extraction of this stone, because death follows in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when the sign is not clear, do not trust the stone, for it does not always leave its mark, if it be broken, it will cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of a fractured skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and jumps up the syfac which is above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scraping and swelling and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes without a wound of the nose or the ear; and sometimes it causes the loss of speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and sometimes with a white moist wound resembling blood clots, and also with a reddish swelling like burn;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign shows you, if you persist in your treatment, draw out the arrow if it is not entangled.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is pierced or hooked is that it is close to the left breast, and feels just as if it were stuck in something hard, do not make it empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow moves just like a worm, and in dark blood without, comes cold and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	its limbs then sense doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that never heals is only without pus coming from the wound, and the swelling increases, and the patient’s complexion changes, and he sighs deeply and vomits profusely.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow tip remains in the covering of the wound, if it is removed, there is great pain and swelling, and deep sighing; and the limb moves abnormally
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow tip is broken or in the stomach, by chance no sign of indigestible meat from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow tip is broken or in the stomach, and there is no sign of feces in the intestines, if there is no hope for recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the bladder stone passes into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it is fractured and the collarbone and the jaw and the shoulder and the elbow and the wrist and the forearm and the leg, and the like, is only saved by numerous precautions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the bladder stone is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have told you before, for in this case you must do something else.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There is one home remedy for this, that is a bladder stone which comes out in the armpit or in the groin.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and on the other side I pulled out the fat of the ear, and it was sane without harm.

taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Thus do thus, until the nails can take hold, and then take it out: if the wound has burst now.</start_of_turn>

Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the nails with which we treat the saiettes are similar to the beak of an oyster, and thus be the form:

des voinnes dou cors communes	From common veins do blood often flow.

Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to remove old blood clots, and to expel foreign bodies.

Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the ancient face, and migraine, and redness.</start_of_turn>

However, I advise that the flame be neither too great nor too small; and the latter is better, for the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn

Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not worth as much as water, and for sode, it is forced out, and for diseases of the face,

et c’est li forme dou flaime:	For the fire cautery:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the veins is aided by the cautery of fire in the swelling of the veins, in the beginning of swelling, in many diseases, in haemorrhoids, in corns, in herpes, and in tumours.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	When the patient’s limb is affected by the fire, the blood is driven out of its vessel by the swelling at its base.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then let the vein be long and widely opened, and hold the blood vessel firmly, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then make the other part in the other vein, and loosen the thread, and strain all the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins from the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the limbs, and dullness and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then open the vein, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are known by this, that they are black, and because they have small veins running black inside them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore one must hold both of them still; and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if the greatest part of the chest has a swelling, and also makes two veins below and above, because this is a similar remedy.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the veins of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of veins that are swollen with the tongue is of help after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the color of the blood is such that if the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and stretches out the tongue, and looks towards every rib, he sees a black vein
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	the blood does indeed flow from one side to the other, and does not rise too high, because these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins often suffer from wounds from which we commonly communicate are sound in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or if they are pierced with any sharp object, such as a flame burning brightly or a subtle olive-shaped thorn as with cuts from trenchant knives, and is called "anesil."
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the size and extent of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame burning brightly if famous, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And must needs be to open the great veins filled with visible blood, which contain great blood and disorder.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for the healing of the small veins, or where there is little yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases such as nausea of the throat, and cough, and pain in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is proper for the healer to remain calm, and to seize the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he seizes the artery and blood spurts out, if the healer is cautious, as I have said before.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be rash with the fire, but must be patient like an ass.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	and if the burn does not clearly manifest itself, then you must believe that you have drawn out too much, and bind another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or do you wish no rain from it, or do you keep in its place the vein filled in the arm: it opens immediately.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the vessel at the flame becomes silent, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see that the limb is moving, if you must stretch out the arm, touch the limb as long as you recognize the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the limb is dislocated, and then stretch out the arm, and hold the vein at the flame silent.</start_of_turn
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the limb swell, for it is the artery: stop immediately.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell high like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor limp, know that it is not an artery: stop immediately.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hastenedly hold your hand over the swelling, and place your thumb along its length, then open your hand if it does not stick, for many times it has happened to me.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	keep the limb still, and leave it alone; do not move the patient unnecessarily. And be careful, for there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it is not stained and it pains, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts because the head is retracting, staunch it without delay.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a sponge of cotton wool, and put it on, and take half of it and put it on well until the other half.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it is not stained, that is good; but if it is, as we have said, powder that stops blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	The bleeding will not be completely stopped in many cases because of the smallness of the wound and the position of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of the vein comes to aid in the treatment of blood clots that are in the chief under the jaw, and in the sides of the body.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basil and cephalic veins, as we have said
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	it is useful because it fills the cavity below the jaw, and if it is not enough, it finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	it swells up and the patient is either stifled or by chance cannot recover;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some homes due to its subtlety, it is certain that you must remove its sensitivity from the instrument that numbs it; and take away the sensitivity of the nerve from your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is long enough.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood from the cephalic vein helps, that it pulls blood towards the head, and helps the veins;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	For the blood of the left hand is not useful, because it is too far from the cephalic vein.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Whatever, it is better to inquire gently at first, and do not grieve if it does not succeed the first time, and we start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance it swells up with some people, when it does not succeed the first time, but do not grieve.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must be conserved in order to maintain health.</start_of_turn
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to prevent future ailments;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the blood be drawn from one of the two veins which are or ought to be: namely, the cephalic, facial, or basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must administer the nourishment at the commencement of vomiting, and after meals, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must administer the nourishment the first or second hour, after twelve or twenty-four hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood that is administered for diseases has no definite measure, but when necessary is in proportion to the degree of urgency in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not permitted to give blood to children under the age of 123, nor to women who have been menstruating for more than four months up until the seventh month
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Blood should not be given to those who have passed 60 years of age
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone feels faint, in whatever way, if it is known that they have a lesser fistula,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a mouth of madness retained, so that the veins do not draw intestines from the excessive humors borne by the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	if there is a mouth of madness retained, so that the veins do not draw intestines from the excessive humors borne by the principal members, do not allow too much meat, neither that which is rotten, for it is fierce, nor hydrops.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if you wish to be cured after a violent passion, vomiting, and discomfort of the belly, and multiple trips to the bath, and sleeplessness, and weeping and groaning, and all the goodness, or by some weapon or poison;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtile the humors, if you are able, with food and drinks and medicines, if you are able to afford them;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter the bath, if nothing hinders, to subtilize the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and keep the vein open from the root up to the third part, as we have said before
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and take care of the work, of the point, of luxury, and of other things like that;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joined, and let the blood be higher than it should be, and wipe the hands once or twice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then it is strange that the limb hangs limply downwards, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot be corrected without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then the hand grasps the limb, until the veins swell and are felt.</start_of_turn>
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the skin with a little oil, and put the thumb of your left hand on that vein below the limb so that the limb becomes stronger.</start_of_turn
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not break and cause injury.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run as quickly as strings to the physician, and if some of them are filled with windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when one puts on the flame, if one takes it away again, and cannot open the vein, then one is in this case.</start_of_turn>
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts the vein, if the wound is too great, because of this one must advise the physician in these matters.</start_of_turn>
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; but if not, one must repeat the process again until the swelling subsides.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is inflamed and the patient is dejected, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Then, in such a case, there will be swelling; do not enter or bathe, and then restart the bleeding when it stops
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	If the wound is small, or if there is doubt that there will be enough blood to staunch the wound, do not hesitate to cauterize the wound directly over the flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and the work must be done carefully, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not immediately renew the bleeding, but apply a pad of lint soaked in oil, because it softens the blood and is held in this limb by the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and in this way administer the oil-soaked lint to staunch the flow of blood, so that the blood vessels may remain closed.</start_of_turn>
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	this also makes the limb tremble and swell, when it is applied to the limb; if it is left on for too long, it will split apart.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	and if there comes a large abscess, which has happened many times, even when the vein is only slightly damaged, or the incision is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put on the wet sponge and a little charcoal on the wound, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And remember that you must do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days, no blackness or greenness, if it does not harm me;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put nothing of aloe or mastic resin in juice of calamus, mustard, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of blood in the armpit: put your hand there, and if you feel the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave me alone; do not place anything further on that which we have already said, for by chance in court without an artery; but make it thus: apply pressure dry to endure the wound, then treat it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark without, if you leave it as long as it is red; and if you see it large, if you leave it as long as it is subtle; and if it is too thick, if you leave it cool.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is proper for the blunt and strong, and for those who have the mastery of blood extraction, to make the wound larger and the flame wider;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak, do the opposite, make it healthier rather than worse, and must do so by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is useful for the evacuation of blood and the compression of nerves, and is worth more than if the blood were long but not wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for him whose body needs blood, it is proper to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is exhausted, two or three times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, if you mix beforehand with blood clotted in olive oil, or in aromatic olive oil with spices, if like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it swells with blood, after the issue of moisture of blood, if it is expedient that it be treated with charcoal, and fragrant oil subtile.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees the arm going pale again, and is well another time, if expedient, when it is full of great blood, that it recover itself and recover itself, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has stiffness, if he is well, should wait at least thirteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself well in other parts, if he must be well again, should wait at least two days or three days.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the limb that is already swollen, which causes fever; if you can drain away a great quantity, and expand the opening as much as it bleeds;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then you must not drain out the blood more than is necessary, otherwise it will not heal.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often occurs when the patient is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not think that I am blind when you see him loosen his arm, and do the same thing a second time, for the wound is closed, and you must press firmly upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the arm widely, because that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it as long as it remains stable a second time; or you should touch the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen at the wound comes out,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And put upon it a little of oil and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain me, until the swelling is gone.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to draw out blood a second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is saved in place of the vein of the head for this reason that it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And thus with the blood, if the patient grasps his hand in warm water, so long as the foam is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it must be bound firmly, so that the vein opens easily, and let it remain so for a while.</start_of_turn>
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the hand remain in warm water until the blood has clotted sufficiently;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	but if it swells up, do not remove the hand from the water, for more is risked thereby.</start_of_turn>
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the blood of this vein is more precious than all the others, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood of the right forearm is worth for all diseases of the liver, and that is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein is freed, if we see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the limb is sound throughout, and you grasp it with all your might, if it does not grieve you;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not fear too much, for the nerves are all loosened from their sheath.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then reattach the limb quickly, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as a skilled physician, if you put oil and lint on the wound to stop bleeding, and do this diligently.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of a mouse, and do everything as I have told you regarding the wound.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the armpit is worth for all diseases that are in the chest,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the armpit is worth for all diseases that are in the chest, such as maladies of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the reins, and ulcers and old wounds, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this blood is that if the patient has been suffering from acute pain in the chest and has rubbed over the belly until it turns pale,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the belly is pale, and there is discharge of urine from below the joint of the arm; and the veins are swollen from the elbow downwards with much urine.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Healthy the joint is neither too dry nor too wet, but in the middle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you ward off the nerves that are dry, and keep it moist like when you are grasping; and let the flame be gentle.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved without pain, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you must do it a second time, because the first attempt was salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same on the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The groin of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its blood is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for blood that has clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And its quality of blood is if the patient lies or sits, and is strained below the ankle three times two, twisting.</start_of_turn
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open; and if it does open, if the same happens in all the ways that you can, and through the body.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to leave the hair as it is, for it is strong and easily replaced by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	If you do not manage it, if some rain falls from the sky or the wind blows, towards the little toe, and you are careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	then do as much as you can to stop the bleeding, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton wool; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuum therapy.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc.ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Ventouses are made of horns, or hair, or wool; and the dressing is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting only.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the dressing which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done with great heat, or simply by cutting
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	or the one is at great heat, or the other is with the collar tight;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And thus with others on both coasts of the neck; and the windpipe is loosened from the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the windpipe is loosened from the jaw; and the windpipe on the eyebrows;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the windpipes are loosened from the arms; and the windpipes from the legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the windpipes from the wrists; and the pulse does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And for this reason, I do not fear it, as when we draw blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And therefore I do not fear it, as when we draw blood from a vein; and it is not to be administered with any fire or heat, in any disease that comes from congestion, until all the humors are evacuated.</start_of_turn>
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of a disease it is necessary to administer it, or by custom, if the medicine is given at the beginning of the month or at the end, and if you mix it with honey and every ten days.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they must vomit, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if such ones have swelling and redness on their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and under the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have blood in their mouths, and have lost their tongues, and vomit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if such ones think, and see by blood and sweat and urine and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is wet and moist, we command the patient to abstain from food for two hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the physician helps with the pain of the head … that comes with these eyes, and it cannot be stopped until after the evacuation of all the lymph.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	except when this emptying is in place of the cephalic blood,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	except when it is used by someone with a cold complexion or who has chatharre, for this causes them great suffering;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it must be used cautiously, only in those who have or suffer from cold fevers.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if he who is well is made aware of the danger, he must promptly put the ventouse one place further down on account of the fear of danger.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction cup is at the nape of the neck instead of the blood vessels, and for this reason it is worth expanding to the utmost extent.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and concerning the fissure of the windpipe, and the swelling, and the distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and must be pressed, for if it is held too tightly, it causes obstruction of the throat or the stomach or the chest.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The windsings cause as much pain in the chest as at the root of the teeth, and swelling, nausea, and strangulation, and pain at the base of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is in lieu of the blood of the vein; and you must command the patient to express his hand to put it in, that he does not compress the artery, and does not let blood flow irregularly.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windsings cause such suffering in the chest as in mouth disease, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in lieu of the ailments of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the spleen are just as much a cause of disease as two veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the patient not to fear too much pain, because it is normal, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is so severe that it causes swelling of the underlying tissue, and diseases of the bones; it is therefore necessary that the suction should be large and strong, and have a good grasp; and in case it should slip, it will cause great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds of the thighs are so painful that they draw blood from all parts of the body, cause ancient pains of the groin, and swelling of the belly and testicles; and lead to the loosening of bones; and are in consequence of these three sophenes and two dislocations, and all these things loosen the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction is to put it on empty first, and then gradually add tension, and put it on firmly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the flesh red and swollen, and see the colour of the blood; then let go, and put the suction back on, and take care of the position of the body, for there are some who have a bad temper and are clumsy: if you should only wound once, you will cause great wounds and deep wounds; and do it cautiously.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, it can be wounded three times: the first time to open the great vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is not large, it can be wounded three times: the first time to open the great vein. And if its veins swell with blood, it is sufficient to do so once.</start_of_turn>
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If its veins swell with blood, if we repeat this too often; and if its flesh is thick, if it is perceived to be pierced, then it must be left alone.</start_of_turn>
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is appropriate for those who have thick skin and tough flesh, who have wide pores, to apply poultices of essential oils that are aperitif and dissolving.</start_of_turn
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is thus, with oil of violet, or sweet almond oil, or oil of squash seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If it is thus, with ivy oil, or of pennyroyal, or chamomile, or the like.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, if you take bitter almond oil, or balsamite oil, or oil of angelica, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if you have severe pain and large pores, you must not put any oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash afterwards with a rose-water, or cold water, or vinegar, or cucumber-juice, or porcelain-water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And whoever has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or vinegar, and sumac, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And whoever has excessive thirst, if he rises from wine strong, or vinegar, or broth of rue or chamomile, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and does not take care to keep himself from the wind before and during the bath, but rather after the bath for an hour or so; and does not sleep after the venting.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is known that it must be warned when it is necessary to move and when it is moved.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	When it is necessary to move and when it is moved, it must be warned
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary to move cold things, such as pomegranates and cucumbers and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and greasy medicines, and pastry, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine which is between autumn and new, and mustard, and vinegar, and small oils and herbs;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine which is between autumn and new, and mustard, and vinegar, and small oils and herbs; and when he feels a draft, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is advisable to give no meat at all during a draft, neither pork nor poultry, before or afterwards, in order to comfort the main parts of the body.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	or be discreet about it, but do not let anyone know who is sick;
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the heel, and upon the belly and the bowels and the veins and the anus, for in these members there is no wound which does not suffer from bleeding.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and they are made only to draw blood from a limb to a limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	for if we put them on the limbs when we do not need to draw blood; because of the viscosity which is in the limb, as when we put compresses on the belly and the bowels to make the limb easier.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain, when there is swelling or a fracture, for it removes by its attractive virtue the swelling, or expels the fracture from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus he must elevate it when one places it upon the liver and upon the spleen when there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	These winds are administered empty so soon as they are required; and never are they administered together with fire, and never are they plain with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	if there are diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner we fill the wound with hot water, or water, or where there are herbs that cover this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And there were two palms and a half of barley and there was either cost the entrance to a thousand with a little hole, like when pushing out an arrow.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	Or it be from rain, sweat before if it does not bleed the patient at the putting on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and there was in the middle a twig of thorn or iron, to put on a bandage wound,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there were great and small according to the maladies and the degree of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must put this swelling on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	grip the bandage of silk or linen, and put it through the hole that is in the middle of the swelling,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If the burn is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then put it on the limb and support it as we have said; if you see that the vapor is going up, take away the cup immediately.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and hold the dressing as before, and do it often, if you must.
