En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse, when it is administered for a pleural effusion, at all times, there is no bulge or opening, and is administered only when it is filled with liquid, and is placed on the limb only for a short time;
et c’est li forme:	And thus is the shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	The veins are not to be tied down except in members where it is impossible to apply a tourniquet because of their small size, such as the liver and the spleen, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the bones stripped of flesh, as in the case of bone or marrow, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the liquid if it is that when you find veins that are soft and smooth in sensation, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put a nut in boiling water, until they are soft, and do not have anything in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then either wash the vein and the belly, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the bandage.</start_of_turn>
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are full and warm, and soft, if it is possible to put on a suction cup, put it on, for this is better afterwards.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If this is not possible, if you lift the limb easily, and then with water, moist well, and then press it.</start_of_turn
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb is too late after the bath of cold water, if much, i.e. a cloth of linen in cold water, put on, until the limb is stretched out;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the limb is too long, if put on broken glass or nails, and similar things, until it is stretched out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you take half of a pea and leave it on the limb until it burns, if it is stopped now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more pain, take other baths.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the wounds do not take hold, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or if you insert a needle into it until the wound is closed,
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then keep them in place, as long as they feel the blood flowing; otherwise they will burst open.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, if you sprinkle powder on a wound of aloe and wool gauze, or charcoal, if they will now be quiet.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, dear son, for this chapter is not found in any of the ancient books, nor is it mentioned in any letter
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	because in our land I have never found anyone who has known it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I know of nothing about it, except what I have learned from the ancient books, or from having studied it myself, by experience, and from observing it in my life
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And thus I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated at the end, and I have made clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book contains the sum of the word and the chapters or the learned men put their understanding into it, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proved to know learn this noble art and learn from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or swelling comes to any, if you must quickly heal the patient on one side and on the other, if nothing else hinders, if weakness of the limb, or infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the head of the shoulder is not too taut or too loose; and eat cold broth, such as cold juices, and cheese and herbs, and do not drink wine, eat no fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins of blood; until you have certainty of complete healing, neither swelling of the limb. If the patient returns to normal before the first sign of recovery, he must be given a fresh order.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the bones are broken and begin to heal, if it is known that the patient must not be given meat that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, as with flour mixed with water, and rye, and peas, and beans, and fish, and wine, and other things like these.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For part of the swelling subsides when the bone is more solid and the fracture is more stable.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones that are fractured in various ways do not mend well, neither by themselves nor by soldering according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs; neither are those which are too brittle, like bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But there is no cure, hold tight to the fractured bone, that is, strong tension which has occurred and unites the limb together, until it is firm as it was before; do not move it at all, and for this reason it is recommended to nourish with coarse food, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breakages that go to the marrow, and others by cutting, as with the size of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a breakage with a wound, and a breakage with a small tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the shoulder blade there is its engine, and its own instrument in restoring, according to what it remembers from its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known by the breaking of the bone by that which its blood is clotted, and opens well by force, and some by pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no swelling nor pain, the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have swelling, or fracture, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible for me to do anything but move the hand, but put on medicines that come after this, and then hold it now discreetly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	If the swelling that is bursting goes downwards, and is the junction of these two parts of the joint, it must now be put back in place evenly, so that the abscesses remain alive;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses come, if you leave them without care, as long as the abscesses are calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it gently and steadily in place, and the swelling that has burst will be more easily restored than if it had been pulled out or fractured; and then hold it now discreetly.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones within the bone, if they extend from the thumb to the wrist, or to the hand, or if it is a small limb, or to the elbow, or to the wrist;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	put the limb in its natural position, so that when the fractured parts of the limb are unbound, if you rejoin them at their natural level, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient any further pain or injury.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well support the fractured bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is beautiful, and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come about by their work at incisions and contractions of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is fixed, if the patient is very painful that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, neither turning nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	keep it very steady that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you command him to put himself in a posture where he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him steady that he does not suffer further pain when you restore him.</start_of_turn>
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and that you consider the limb to be broken as I have told you.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limb is broken in various sizes, shapes and forms.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For in such small limbs, as arms and legs and the like: if you cover them with soft linen cloths and blankets;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	For in such great limbs, as hips and thighs: if you cover them with a broad and hard cloth, because the large cloth embraces the whole great limb and restricts it everywhere, so that there is no bulge.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie loosely around the limb, twice or thrice according to the size of the limb, and hold the hand one inch above the break and strain less, than the break itself breaks and lets go one inch of the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the cloth somewhat, so that you take a great part of the limb again, then take another cloth, and turn the dressing around the limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then draw towards the lower part of the break, and hold moderately, not too strong nor too weak, as we said earlier.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the layers of skin some strips of linen or cloth, so that they are all even, and then bind all around with thread, and then put your stitches well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, if put above something soothing the abscess burn, and which strengthens the swelling, and leave it so for several days.</start_of_turn
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your stitches, and let them be half the width of a broad needle resting steadily, or of thread from which we make knots, or of hemp ropes, and let them be as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it must be known that when one sets the bone in place which has a fracture, it must be a larger and wider break than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be of equal length as it ought to be for the limb in general or for its size.</start_of_turn>
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is strained upon the bones just as you did at the first hour, and then bind it loosely with a thread as before the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight is bound, the less; and it must be known that the thread must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and must be of linen wool.</start_of_turn>
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I often see fools do who bind their wounds with linen thread, it is a great error, for the thread will not be even if it is too fine, and it will hold only if there is less space between the stitches.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the threads after the stripping in the flesh, if you put soap on them, I put coarse linen or coarse cloth on them, so that they do not bleed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a wound-cleaner and the bone is fractured, I will speak of the cure for it later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And so, if it cannot be forced out by hand, grasp the broken limb first thing.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it cannot be forced out by hand except after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound; for the wound often comes out before the bone is healed.</start_of_turn>
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and thus, with this old method of packing, to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that is held fast as the walls of a mill, and mix it with abundant eggs, and make this confection, not too fine nor too coarse, and use it. This is the common method of restoring the fracture in many situations, and even among women and young children, for it is neither too tight nor too loose.</start_of_turn
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of packing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley, linseed, laurel, asafoetida, gum arabic, mugwort, and mix them with an egg; mix mirra and aloes with a third of an egg; mix alechil with eight eggs; and grind them all together; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this packing, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other means of supporting that is worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, mix with vinegar three times; mirret and aloe, mix with vinegar eight times three; acaice five times three; arnica ten times three, and grind well, and confit with water or plenty of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other means of supporting that is worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, mix with vinegar three times; mirret and aloe, mix with vinegar eight times three; acaice five times three; arnica ten times three, and grind well, and confit with water or plenty of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of supporting that is worth torsion: take dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Other means of restoring the fracture of the bone and removing the remaining abscess. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violets flowers, wheat flour, one part of rue; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with moist coriander water, or water alone, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Other means of setting is more violent for the first one, when the abscess hardens at the restoration of the limb. Take root of vismalve, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, violets and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; grind and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that we must put something dry and warm on the limb to restore it, such as mirre and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is useful for wound and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions or fennel, and balsam, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of them.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has any movement of his limb; if you do not loosen it by hand for a while.</start_of_turn
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain comes to the limb, or swelling or itching, if you rush and loosen it, and put the limb in place now; take a lighter bandage, a sponge of moist sea-moss, and immerse in water, and lift the limb up, until the itching stops and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry cloth, soaked in water or rose oil, and tie on a bandage, until you are certain of the healing of the wound
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Rest the inflamed limb, and if there is pain, then rejoin the bandage and a little support, and do not bind too tightly; and take care until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain, and swelling around a bone, and if the pain persists, you must support and bind it firmly, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not happen in the limb what we have said, if it does not loosen up within two or three or five or seven days; do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the swelling has gone down, and approach the closing of the wound slowly.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore more restraint than before, and soak the meat, as I have said before; and if you see the limb dry out more than usual, do not attempt to pull out the swelling;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arose, alors, que tu le deslies, qu’il fasse chaud de l’eau chaude, toutes les fois que tu le fais, et ce soit chez quiconque tiers, et fais-la susciter un peu la corde.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	When you loosen it, then, that it makes warm water, every time you do it, and this be it with any third person, make it stir up a little the thread. For by this work, indeed, it often happens that it returns to its place the limb, and this is bad, and if the work is rough, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it violently.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many are the ways of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collar of the bone is fractured throughout to the syfosis which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a chisel or fist; and for this reason it is called this kind of fracture "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or if the spear pierces the bone from the outside inwards, and is called this kind of fracture "absolue"; and is the wound of these great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the nail or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst fracture, which approaches the gut that is beside the bone, or it is on the bone, and is this wound great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is closed in the bone as subtly as a hairpin, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound made or by cutting with a knife, or by thorn, or by anything similar, and it lets a piece of bone go down into the gut, and the limb becomes as limp as if it were hung over a cauldron; if there is something between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this often happens with soft bones or those of children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are many such breaks in these ways that small pieces are detached from them as in stars; and I will speak of them in detail.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these breaks by the loosening above them, by the incisions of the tents, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The like of hair is known by that which when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped over it, if the black break is opened.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, emission of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes watering and reddening, and other similar things in greater or lesser degree, if it does not sense without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any imminent mishap, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling first comes to you, and it is in the armpit, if so, you must remove the bone in front of the wrist from the joint that you must put in place.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you hasten to remove the bone in front of the elbow, so that the bone of the limb is corrupted, then comes the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone breaks as far as to cover the brain, if so, you must make an incision in the wound so that you can see: and take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound more roughly than you can.</start_of_turn
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood comes out with the uncovering of the bone, or with an abscess, hold fast to what is useful and fill the wound with soft cloth soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And keep the abscess quiet until the bone is finally stable, and be sure there is no further bleeding; then begin to close the wound. This is done in two ways: the first way is if the wound is narrow at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another wound that is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And so if you have various sized swellings, some are thin and others are thick, and they are pointed or iron-like; and on their lower parts, do not touch the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and tough, if you must pierce through, even if you administer swellings with poultices, do not make them go beyond the test of the bone; and must have beneath the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must do this several times, for if pieces of bone come to lie in the place of the thickness of the bone, because of the poultices you must give for the test. And this is the form of the two methods of poultices.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put on one poultice over the bone, and twist your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put on another poultice in another place a little later, and do the same all around; then close the incisions of the space between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any other instrument that you have like nails, pincers; and keep your hand away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated, if it is possible, reset the apurture which is loosened from the bone to all other instruments that resemble an incisor, but it must be more tense and flexible than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it leaves nothing of the small bones, no nails, if the bones are slightly fractured; then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is like the Galen method, which is more useful; and the load is very strong, and that is his word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by displacement of muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, you must place the thumb of your injured finger against the flesh, as it is formed:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not cut from one side only, and if the part is rough in the marrow, if you cut towards the bone; then fix with a little mallet above, so that you can slightly bend the bone all around, and take care of the membrane that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is tough against the bone, if the bone is slightly bent, because we must well sense the pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks but does not pierce the skin, the bone is simply cut through from above; and there are small pieces remaining. If you wish to remove the rough edges, you must have various quantities of the blunt rasp available, so as to smooth each piece according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are before great rasps, and afterwards more subtle, and you do not cease doing this until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle breaks, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its situation; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not thoroughly studied this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the face is discovered, take one drape of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drape of linen doubled in half or in quarters, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you please, that you do not damage the face, then administer from above another linen, and do not bind it more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound steady only
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one or two hours, until the swelling of the abscess is diminished, then take it off, and administer medicines such as root of chamomile, flour of barley, incense powder, and herbs; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer accordingly appropriate medicines with a pleasant taste.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And beware that the wound be perfectly closed, that thou leave it neither open nor reassembled with a bow, for when a bow is reassembled upon the head of the cerebrum, if it be crooked and firm, it brings great harm to the patient; for when one sets upon it any biting thing, if it is not held down by something else.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed, therefore, if no other mishap befalls the patient, as we have said, if there be doubt concerning it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other force comes forth from the medicine which we have set upon, that some part of virtue has, if you must take, a part of honey, and two parts of rose oil and glue one drapel; and put it upon the surface.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the treatment in the manner of cures that it is allowed, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then comes the treatment in the manner of cures that it is allowed, as long as it is sane.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, if it is possible, to drink a little wine or extract from the bone, and put equal pressure on this fracture within your index finger and thumb, as long as it does not return to its natural figure.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the limb, and cannot come from below, if you can, put the limb even with the top of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is three-fourths of the way up, if you make another, and hurry to restore the limb first, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not done, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the limb has subsided, then you must try to bandage the limb, if the fracture is in the limb itself
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must break it again somewhere else, if the fracture is there; and be as strong as you can in your attempts to fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say no restorer must moisten the tents in the burrow, and must die each one for himself. It does not seem to me that this is good, but it must be that they are moistened in the making of an egg-bread and flour; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Never put feathers of a goose instead of tents, and if there is any soft drape about, and if you keep the pincer, and blow on the patient among them; or do as you will see.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out while you are working, if you put some lint or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in some linseed oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the afterpains do not come, if you put on a plaster by force, of hempseed flour, and incense powder, confirmed with the yolk of an egg, then put on soft bandages, and do not bind tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture does not break through, and it is broken into many pieces, if you have available instruments, then draw out the fragments, and suture the wound, and treat with healing herbs, and oil, as with plasters and bandages available.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no swelling in the wound, if you can cure with stitches, and put on cold compresses, as long as it is necessary.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the route of the mandible.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is routed downwards, and there is no wound, and the fracture is only slight, and is not broken thoroughly, except for the curvature inwards, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the outer part, to bite down with the thumb of the affected hand in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take the thumb of the right hand, and grasp the fracture lightly, and hold it apart with the other hand, and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if it is necessary to administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes pain, or a fracture, if they are strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken jaw cerate on and put over it a double drape; and put over the drape a large staple well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it to the muscle as you please, and command the patient to rest and eat lean meat.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure is deformed, if the bone is fractured at the third part, and then reset it to its place; then put on a plaster cast, of pounded powder with much egg or oatmeal, after you have set the cerate; and put on the plaster clean linen, and if the plaster is loose, and the patient’s condition does not worsen, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the patient has a wound that comes open, if we have already said many times what we have said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, award that no part of the bone is fractured; if slight of the bone has escaped, cover it with something that covers it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is severe, if the swelling has gone up with flame as you desire.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have united all these parts, and there is no longer any displacement, if the wound is large, put on some dressings that cover it, in order to prevent suppuration, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la forcele	forcefully</start_of_turn>
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two manners: when it is broken and loosened in four places, and there are fragments, and that is the lightest to restore; or if there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is when the wound faces downwards, take two assistants, so that one holds the limb where the force breaks; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then set the break even, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of lead or linen, and be large as you need; and stretch and hold the forcele, and strain the ball with your hand, so that you set the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to support the head of the shoulder, when it comes out of place, if you must know, the patient lies supine on his belly, and place the shoulder blade between the nipples, and keep the minister there until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris there, if you must know, make an incision there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join together by any means, if the socket is at one of the incisors you have; but that you place between the shoulder blade and the breast bone this instrument to keep the wound open.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	It appears like a spoon, and is not crooked, and should be as wide as it seems necessary, according to the size of the bone and the position of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the afterburn, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the afterburn, if you use a bandage and pins according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the afterburn comes, if it is moist, apply oil of roses, rue and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stiffness of the bone, when it has wounds and is swollen, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the meal of wheat flour and egg yolk, and put on stockings loosely, and put a splinter below the armpit if you must.</start_of_turn
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great bandage of a palm of a broad size, and put two layers of drapeil over the wound and cover it; then take a needle of the thinnest kind of two sizes broad and long, and encircle that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is pendant.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Then put the needle on the bulge, and turn the bandage on the collar, and drain the liquid from the wound, and drain the wound from the painful side; and hold the edges apart, and when you see that the ligature holds the bulge steadily, and you clearly see that the needle does not move from the broken bone, if you reward generously, and if you restrain them.</start_of_turn>
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	Then make the patient lie on his back, and put under him one little pillow to support the wound; if you align the break of the arm with the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not release it until it is well healed, for about twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then resume the traction, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the traction, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then resume the traction, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, and the bone, make do with the forceps to subdue the abscess at its source.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, and the bone, make do with the forceps to subdue the abscess at its source.</start_of_turn>
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this often happens; but it often breaks from excessive force. And when it is broken in two, if it declines to yield, and the patient feels great pain, and has no other remedy, then vomiting blood, and opening the wound in the broken bone, and the like.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that if the patient lies soven on his back, and puts one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and assemble the ribs of the two costae with your hands, and gently put everything in its place as it should be; then put on bandages and bandage the outside of the bone with fine salt, or some other soft matter, and cover with a cloth, and bind the whole thing around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the patient slowly on his back, and strain gently, and praise for a whole hour when it is loosened, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if it seems to loosen, because of corrosion or because of inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are in a hurry, loosen it, and scrape the dressing, and treat what caused the wound; then reinforce the dressing, and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the bones.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Bones that break in the chest do not come forth except after a great swelling behind the back, and at the head downwards; and they do not yield forth except for that which makes them slippery; and one feels them well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture in its place, as it should be. And then put on the dressing and bind it with a bandage, if you have need of it
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the bones is downward towards the belly, if it causes great pain, and swelling, like blood, for the bone points the belly; and there is vomiting, and all together there is great loss of blood, which is a grievous matter, and many have died from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push back the wind.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after eating hot food, which is harmful, does not go away.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If it comes, let it be so.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should not put compresses on the body to dry it, for this is like reason; however, there is doubt that the compress will not draw out the moisture from the body due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that of nowhere must cover the limb with greasy wool, and put on tenses between the ribs in order to measure equally the hour round, then either cure with the treatment of pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the rib, and there is doubt to the patient, if you must cut above the broken rib, and you must put in instruments to hold the flesh; then you must break the bone gently, and drain slightly, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure with sponges, until it is healed. And if an abscess comes, if you put on greasy cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and cure while the limb remains above the abscess, and do not stay on the rib or it must, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of bones in the neck, or that it rains; and the same with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to no avail, and you know not whether it will be healed or not, if you take heed when you see its hands limp and fleeing and dying, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel it. Such is death in many positions, and if you move them and feel well when you strain and point, such is that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be healed, if we put in cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when such things happen to the spine, and you know not whether it will be healed or not, if you take heed when you see its pieces are softened, and when an accident happens that is in the hands or on the back, with a violent wind and vomiting without volition; and when it is bound on its belly, vomiting without volition. And when it is bound on its back and it sees blood flowing, if it cannot move. Such is death: if it does not work diligently in its cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not occur, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if such an accident does not occur, it is the lighter thing. If there is swelling at the apex, put on rose oil or oil of nutmeg on the spine; until it is calmed. Then put on one of the comforting and drying patches, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is fractured, it is necessary to cover over the wound with a bandage; and then to unite the two ends of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, and cure it with ointment that is healing, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "fracture of the heel", if it is in your left hand, put it equal to the right hand in your pocket, and put the bandage and the splint on, if you need them; then strain it, and if there are bones that are loosened, keep it still, and unite them, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if there is no sign of improvement even after a long time, and the limb is drooping downwards, and there is pain at the root, and swelling around that which breaks
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above the fracture, until you reach the fracture; and keep the limb in such a way that the fracture is properly aligned; and if the fracture is only at the shoulder, put it in its natural position, until it is perfectly healed
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or is drooping downwards, make the patient sit up on his belly, until the restoration of the fracture is visible.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have placed the limb even, if you place upon the socket a peg of wood or bone, and hold the flesh still, if it does not move; then use the hand of the patient to support the cost, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to rest on his side, or on his back
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If swelling comes, if it does not touch, until the swelling has subsided, and place what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no other mishap; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And thus take two fingers of the hand and grasp the limb above the socket; then hold the patient above a seat; then gently bend the arm over the fist, as far as it can go without causing pain; and put under the fist a cushion or something similar; then put the thumbs of both hands together, so that the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his heel, and bind the arm to his collar, and command two assistants to hold what is above the dislocation with their hands, and the other to hold below all the bones, and stretch the skin to the part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the extraction is too violent, strain the limb.i. the bones that are close to the elbow and on the elbow itself. Extend the thumbs of the attendants to their sides. If the elbow is close to the shoulder, put in li. the middle bone from the shoulder and the other towards the elbow. If the elbow is towards the wrist, put in li. the lighter bone, with effort, as long as the elbow is level on both sides. Then put the bone back in its place if possible, and strain, if necessary, for the wound does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the wound comes out again, do not strain for more than three days. Put on a thick bandage of linen and oil of roses until the wound is quiet; then strain, and the way to strain is to put in the dressing under the elbow, then reassemble the arm on the splint, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest; put on the bandage and strain on the splint and the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without anything hindering it, or without breaking the bones.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and put under the bone a splint that is wider and stronger than the others, and have between the splints a space of two finger-widths, so that one splint passes over the elbow two finger-widths beyond the other; then strain on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the shoulder blade slipping and the limb is drawn out of its place, as we have said, while restoring the limb, if you doubt the completeness of the cautery, let it adhere until the seventh day, as we have said; then watch for seven days to see if swelling or pain does not arise in the limb, or if the limb does not regain its natural movement. If the pain persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing happens, if more than two days have passed, and the patient is lying on his back with his hands on his stomach; put the limb in a cushion made of even wool, and watch for an hour or two to see if the limb is still crooked or if the ligaments are slack. If the pain persists, as we have said.
de la brisure du bras	And if the fracture of the arm has happened, you must first of all set the limb in its place, and keep it still in this way for as long as necessary; and you must take care that the limb does not move too much, for this would cause more damage.  And you must feed the patient well during this time, and give him medicine for the pain.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.
