The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna." One is small and is like a nail that supports the pouch; and the other is large and is like a socket, towards the little finger. By chance the large humerus alone breaks, or the small, and by chance both together break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small humerus breaks, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large breaks, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they break together. If only the small humerus breaks, if the limb is slightly extended, and made even
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large humerus that breaks, if the limb is strained more strongly; and it is stretched over the thumb, and holds the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small should be lower than the other two, and either the patient should be crossed over on itself, or the thumb should be in front of it higher, than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the limb slowly from the shoulder to the wrist, or to the elbow, and another assistant to the other side. And then set the limb in its natural position, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If it breaks into pieces, if you put some [material] into its place, and if there is none that prick [it] now, you will not be able to restore it to its place, even if you leave it there and the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If it breaks into pieces, as I have mentioned in the previous chapter; take the treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If at the commencement of the restoration blood comes out through the incisions, if you glue [it] with a bandage of cerote made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too thick or too thin; and tie [it] with a bandage above the wound so that the blood vessels are not irritated. Then put the bone back in place and put the bandage back in its place. Pour on puts the plaster, with a great deal of egg-white, because one must put the pins in; put in the pins that are more numerous at the fracture and a little wider than the others; and that the wound must have enough pins to hold it in place. The pins should be of flaxseed, neither too thick nor too thin, as I have said. And leave the bandage moist and soft, not too hard or too brittle; and the thread that is used to tie it should be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as I have said. Reward the limb and the surrounding area after a few days.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If new troubles arise in the limb, as for example itching that arises in the limb, you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching subsides; and then let the limb rest still. And then repeat the stretching, and if the tendons are softened and the bones loosen, and similar things, if necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the swelling does not come back to the limb, because it is too tight, you must soften it somewhat, and leave it alone for some days, until the swelling goes down, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said help the patient, if not loosening them for twenty days or even longer, then you must hold the patient’s hands to his chest, and keep his chest even, and prevent him from moving or eating, and let him sleep on his back; and give him nourishment every thirty days or so, according to the compositions and constitutions of the virtues.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de la main	From the break of the wrist
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the break of the wrist, there are often breaks at the base of the thumb and index finger. It happens often that there is only blood flow left in many cases.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the wrist is broken or bruised, if it is suspected that the patient has suffered a fracture, one must hold the hand steady and keep it straight in front of them; then place the hand on the extended cloth and extend the broken bones, and put them in their proper place; and put on the dressing and bandage, if there is no swelling, and put on a splint according to the degree of displacement; and be covered with a bandage.</start_of_turn
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is at the edge of the limb towards the belly of the bone, make a loop of bandage and command the patient to stretch it over their broken limb; then tighten with a long bandage, and put on a splint as large as the limb, and tighten it as much as it is convenient.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is on the side, then you must put a splint on the top and another on the bottom, so that the hand is fully extended; then bind it tightly around the hand and pack the linen between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not arise from either side, if it is on the pouch, if it is equal, as it should be; and strain it with the splint, and if you see that it does not move, put a right-angle splint below to raise the fracture, and do not move it; or if the fracture is elsewhere, as on the index finger or any other, if it is equal, and bind it with two strong threads that follow; or bind them together tightly, as much as you can, or put on a splint, as with a pouch; and take care in restoring and positioning the burnt area, and secure what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and one can see it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is in the marrow of the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the thigh, if either the upper ligament towards the heel or the lower ligament of the fracture is stretched; and in the same way if it is close to the knee, and then either the lower ligament of the knee or the upper extension; then put the thumb of the hand over the bone equal to its natural position, and then put the bandage, and bind it, if there is no displacement.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a boil above, if you leave it calm and return to your work and your treatment; the dressing is made in a rough manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the swelling, that is, a bandage twice or thrice, and in this way keep the excess blood in check, then twist the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail; and hold there for a while a thread about a league long between the hip and the limb, leaving the groin bare, and bring the thread to the top of the limb; then twist on the limb and on the hip the bandage, and put on the outer bandage, and put a pin on the bone of the limb; then use the eighth between the limb and the hip of coarse cloth to make equal the tension, and start to tie two or three knots on the bandage; and the more you go up the swelling, and the less you strain; then when you have put in two or three threads that you have left between the limb and the hip, and have put in two pins that are below, then withdraw the thread from the top of the limb, as long as you see that it comes out from below; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it be, and do not come to any other swelling or bruise or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling, if it bursts, and addresses what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them; and if we are unable to do so, it is necessary to cut the limb open, and drain; and cure as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the limb broken in this case when it is set, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made thereupon, do not be afraid to make the patient suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And if the limb is set in the space of one or two days, or less or more, according to the variety of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of genoil
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	There are often breaks in the street of genoil, but it rains many times. And if it breaks, it is not more than a tear, or a hole, and there is pain, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if restoration is to be made, put the round end back into its place, until it is firmly assembled; then place the plug and insert a round pin, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then restore all the other arrangements that we have mentioned before, such as cautery and the like; if you put into practice each of the precautions that we have mentioned, as long as it is necessary.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if restoration is to be made, put the round end back into its place, until it is firmly assembled; then place the plug and insert a round pin, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then restore all the other arrangements that we have mentioned before, such as cautery and the like; if you put into practice each of the precautions that we have mentioned, as long as it is necessary.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And if restoration is to be made, put the round end back into its place, until it is firmly assembled; then place the plug and insert a round pin, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then restore all the other arrangements that we have mentioned before, such as cautery and the like; if you put into practice each of the precautions that we have mentioned, as long as it is necessary. As for the breaking of the limb which has two bones, one of them is called the "muscle" and the other the "fossa"; and there is every chance of breaking it as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is made in exactly the same way as for the arm, and the work is exactly the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are fractured together, the limb is twisted in every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted forward
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a great bone is fractured, if one feels great pain and sees it well fractured; and the limb is twisted. Therefore bring extension, and set it even, and bind the limbs evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, that the extension is less and lighter; and adjust accordingly to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, if you take .ij. strips of coarse wool that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the foot; then wrap in .ij. layer of lint from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle; and with this binding the limb will not slip forward or backward, and that is good; and no one should administer any other bandage that is as long as the limb, and if there is swelling, and put the limb in position to prevent movement, and do this at the fracture or wound; and move each joint of the limb to see if there is any displacement or other accident; if there is, cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones that is inside.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in bones that are inside there is no fracture ever and two must be left, and there is only certainty in many situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in these bones, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put so much pain on the limb that it would be as if it were flying towards you, and then put your limb on the ground, where the bones are lifted up, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put the dressing and bandage on, and put a little bandage under the belly of the limb, and bind the limb steadily, and cover it with a cloth or other things as you deem necessary.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if you loosen the limb, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said, do two things with the hand. Then put at the break end a splint of the length of two fingers, and make it wider; then put on the thumb that I have mentioned, and strain it immediately. If there are three or more breaks, break each one and put on at each break an splint according to its quantity, enveloped in a layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the break. Keep the thumb resting on the chief of the thumb over the belly of the thumb as long as it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things I have said concerning other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if she sits enlarged, then lean her forward; and hold her by the back; then fill the belly with cotton, and put as much on it as on a stone; then pull out the woman, and keep her back and front; and then jump the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the belly, and bring back the bone with the stone; and when she vomits, if the stone is in the cotton, and when she has vomited, she will recover; and such is the case for thirty days or more: if the fracture is restored, and you see it, take a bladder of elderberry, and tie a string to the navel, and pour all the bladder into the belly; then blow up the string as much as the bladder is emptied: the belly will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	When the bone of the shoulder of a man or a woman is broken, if it is restored as we have said concerning the bone of the thigh; and these fractures which are not obvious are seen only by him who has studied them and used them, and who has read my book. For the fracture signifies in many cases the right way of restoration: otherwise.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is broken, take a gooseberry and put it in the groin; then wrap it around with a bandage, and leave it for two or three days, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	From a break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has suffered a fracture with wound, even if it is great, if like the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be sound now, if as we have said the wounds testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, if the vitriol remain, if you have nothing else, then resume the restoration of the fracture in this way, or that, if the pus comes out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes out, if you leave the restoration until tomorrow, while the pus is calmed, and do not touch neither a third nor a quarter, for you will risk coming to a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks open is appears above the joint discovered, then you must know that you must hold it firmly in your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to hold it equally in your hands, if the handle of this instrument which is of iron, which is three or four fingers long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it must be grasped that it grasps three or four fingers, according to what is necessary in the bruise of the wound; and let it be round and have a large head, so that it does not press against the compression on the limb at your work, and be firm before, and large from the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called a "palainche" because it must be known that when the limb is crooked the bone must be placed above the apparent head of the bone; and once it has been placed, it must be even so that one side encounters the other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, if you must cope with the head of the bone, as long as the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone as we have said, if you have grasped with a curable instrument, such as an incision or hook, at your will; then remove that which remains embedded in the bone, leaving only the rough fragments and small pieces of marrow.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored, and the patient experiences great pain afterwards, it is because it is not in its natural position. If you do nothing, it will swell. I.e. cover it with black vinegar and keep it covered; do not put any cerote or other material on the wound as this will cause putrefaction and corruption. Then administer medications as soon as the bone is restored, and leave the wound uncovered, covering only the surrounding area according to the size of the wound. Be careful not to strain the wound with breaking. Many times this has been the cause of death among fools, who have caused death or damage to many patients.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is small or large, and you doubt that there is any serious underlying cause, as we have said, and you experience pain, if it is not necessary to administer medications; but cover loosely around the wound with a thick cloth, and bind. And when you see afterwards, i.e. after an hour or two, that the swelling has increased at the wound, if the bone that you placed over the wound has become soft, and there is blood coming from the wound, put on healing ointment for wounds, such as tetracycline and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you draw the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is soldered and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it must be that the limb be put back in place gently as if it had never been dislocated
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it recurs, and cannot be soldered but returns to its place, with slight pieces of bone, for it must be that you wish to treat the wound with care, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if there is a fistula or other corruption of the limb, if it must be cured, according to what is said in the previous chapter. And when the bone is broken, and opened on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the great limbs, if it is not treated, for often death comes from this; but leave it until it has bled for about twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; or leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out from the beard.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Hair that comes out from the beard comes out often after the heat of the bath, even when it is close to the joint, and it is a helpful sign to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot make the limb move naturally.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that it should not slip: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, make sure that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stiff wine or with much egg or with vinegar; and put them on the wound in bandage, and strain it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is healed; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the nodulation is bony; or you strain on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it can harden all the swellings under the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it is necessary to break it, if the swelling under the limb is great, and make the excess visible; or do not remove it until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is restored, and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any fault: because it was too tightly bound and could not be loosened; or because there is too much binding, and it cannot move smoothly; or because of numerous ligatures; or because of too great a movement, not in its entirety; or because there is much blood in the limb, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient move about, and tighten the limb, until the swelling is diminished in him; and give him baths, and make him comfortable and cheerful; then put on a bandage over the limb, so that the bandage will draw out the great swelling, and the blood flows steadily, until the limb is restored to its natural position; and bring back to its usual shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After the disease, the limb is twisted.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is fractured open, and the limb is deformed, although it has returned to its natural position: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be fractured anew, and many have had this done in our land; this work is blamed, and there follows great evils, and by chance death; although if the swelling and torture are fresh, if one believes they have arisen from warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, like ivy leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and it makes one apply a soft dressing, like good aquaintance, and take the nourishment of ivy, and confirm with butter of geline or oil of sesame, and apply the dressing on; or one takes fat figs, and grinds them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never is the bone fractured by continuous rubbing with moist hands. And let there be provided movement for the limb during the night.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, it is necessary to cover the wound with a bandage, making an incision slightly deeper; and to put padding and a support in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no avail, if you must now restore its place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, if the limb is swollen, and by chance when it is reset there are points on the limb; for this reason one must not move it while it is swollen: many times this has brought on vomiting and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this happens, if you make the patient more comfortable, then let him rest, until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb high and with oil, and gently massage it, and cure each limb as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the shoulder to the foot
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The teeth are loosened and the jaws are dislocated in two ways: when they are united by the root of the teeth; or when they are entirely loosened and hang towards the chin, and cause the saliva to flow from the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself several times
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	and if it is entire and accompanied, it is necessary that you immediately reset it, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such manner that the minister grasps the head of the patient and beholds one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is of three parts; and the other hand must be thrust out, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the mark be equal, until it returns to its place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns crooked, even though the two mandibles are together, if they arose from hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed with a gentle touch, if you put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and wax, then bind them loosely with linen.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient lies on his back, and his arms are placed between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, do not attempt to pull them out, but gently seize the meat, until the pain is eased, and keep the jaws closed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then eat slowly and gently, and do not work too hard to open your mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not manage to be put back in their place at a single hour, and are not firmly converted to their roots, if in comes fever and customary nausea, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death is the consequence, in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the snare.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The snare does not know how to unhook from its cost, and is devalued once it is released, and one can feel it.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the patient lies supine on his back and extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then put on the dressing and bandage, and restrain it;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And thus the dislocation is returned, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder is dislocated only by two means: firstly, when it slips from the socket downwards; and secondly, when it slips from the head downwards; and sometimes from the upper part, and this is bad.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	It does not slip behind the shoulder, nor does it slip from the nerves; and it often slips downwards towards the socket, just as is the case with those who have too little flesh; for those who have enough flesh, it slips with pain and returns with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there happens to be a fracture or dislocation, and if the shoulder is bruised with a hard blow, it is dislocated by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is obvious. You must be certain that the dislocation has been completely remedied; only then should you begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	Dislocation is known when it is tilted towards the rump, and it distinguishes between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their divergence an obvious difference.</start_of_turn>
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and at the head of the shoulder there is a socket, and the ball of the shoulder touches the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bow; and the patient is unable to move his arm to its place, or to move in any way.</start_of_turn
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is displaced upwards, if it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation is not without force to restore it when it is new, or when the limb is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the physician holds the painful limb high up, then puts his thumbs under the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully high up; and the physician holds the limb and stretches it high up, because of this it comes out immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come out as we have said before, if it is to be known that the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the physician must give nourishment soothing and comforting, as for example decoction of alum and fennel and honeycomb in water, and must be given;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then either rest the patient on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of linen equal, not too soft nor too hard, then put the hand of the limb on the cushion, and hold the shoulder joint firmly, and treat the painful limb.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister holds the patient's head firmly in place, so that it does not move downwards; when the dislocation has returned immediately, and if you see that it remains fixed in this manner,
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and if it is that you make it known, that is to say, that which is greater than the patient; and be firm on the side of the cost, and hold the shoulder away from the patient's buttock, and keep the buttock high, so that the patient hangs down from the armpit.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister grasps the patient's arm downwards towards the abdomen. And if the patient is too light, if you put anything heavy with him, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And in another way, we must hold the arm firmly: like a nail long in the earth, from which the bone is as round as a ball, neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then put some soft dressing on the patient, but that it should have a soft drape over, and that the patient should sit at a long distance; then extend the hand forward from the other side, and the joint will return to its place without pain
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, if you do this cure: take one thumb and two fingers of good size, which has the head round to enter into the socket, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the shoulder, draped with a cloth that will not irritate the patient, then put his hands on the patient's buttocks; extend your arms over the patient's long arm, and hold the shoulder at the arm's root, and put your arm on the wrist of the hand, and put the hand on the first space of an elbow of a large size, and extend the lower hands, or leave the forearm hanging down on the other side: the shoulder is now in its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in its place, in whatever way, if you put his buttocks on a sphere of wool equal in size, then put the shoulder pad firmly with a powder of wheat, with incense and balm of egg, on the entire shoulder and around, then strain from the buttocks immediately, and turn the limb over the shoulder, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands immobile.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he keep moving, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal better; and then move more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the dislocation is forced from its place by moisture, or for some other reason, if you must administer cauteries to the two pierced parts, if it is placed before or alongside the cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it lasts for seventeen days, and the dislocation does not hold, and cannot raise the upper arm, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the dislocation will never heal in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the elbow, and the arms, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and another support is administered; and it is cured as long as it is sound.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.

And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.

Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And it must be known that if it is possible to restore it again as before, when the limb is relaxed, grasp the hand with your two hands and spread the arms apart, and bend the fingers according to the pain of the joint, forward and backward, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and press from the root of the bone that is loosened.</start_of_turn
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it by two ministers, if it does not move during extension, then turn the arm from the shoulder downwards; then cover it with a long and wide bandage.

When it is in its place, if you put on dry compresses with an egg yolk, and the limb becomes strained, and you bend the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for some days, then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you detach the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold firmly, recommence the displacement and reattach the limb, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then detach it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If there is pain after the joint is repositioned, and it moves, bathe and rub the area thoroughly, and press until the pain is gone; or put a poultice of fat mutton grease on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove the poultice and let the limb move naturally
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	When it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then enter or bathe; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see that it is better, put on warm salves soaked in butter, and strain on it; if it returns to its natural position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand has loosened, and the return is slight, more so than in other joints, so it must be forcibly returned to its place immediately, while it is still loose, and even if there is swelling or if there is a wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And thus you must hold the painful limb over a table, and extend the limb, and look that it is even, until it has reached its place.

If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, make the patient rest their hand face down on the table, and their gaze rest their hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If this does not occur, if the strain of soothing supports postoperatively remains, and you leave it in its place, let it resume its natural position.</start_of_turn>

et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	neither must he be forced to do anything except to keep the hand still, and must not be strained in any way; for if the nerves are severed or the veins are cut, nothing else is of any use.</start_of_turn>

de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the arm bones.

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the loosening of the scapula from the back.

When the scapula of the shoulder or the collarbone is loosened, or if there are several dislocations, and there is no remedy, for the patient's life is hurried.</start_of_turn>

des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The hip joint and shoulder joint never dislocate except for dislocations alone, never if like other joints; and the joint of the thigh is damaged in three parts: front and back, and front and back; the more inward it is, the more it is damaged in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And if it is known that the dislocation has occurred within the limb, when one joins the diseased limb with the tendon, if it is longer and the diseased knee is greater than the sound knee, and the diseased limb cannot bend as much as the sound limb at the knee;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And thus is the cause of this displacement from the apophysis of the bone, for in this case the head of the humerus comes out of its place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this displacement is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this displacement is that if the limb is well placed according to the completion, although it is not doubled at the knee with pain, if one sees that it is done too violently, it cannot be done immediately and is delayed, it retains the urine, swells the belly, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes. If this semblance of dislocation recurs, if it is an old dislocation and does not move according to its setting, if there is no remedy; then I advise you to have suspicion.</start_of_turn>
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you hurry that you return the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other remedy.</start_of_turn

de la dislocation dou genoil	And if it rests for two or three days, then loosen it and place the bandage upon it; and if you see that they are even, if strained as before, leave them for two days. Then loosen it and make it bleed gently until the limb is comfortable.

de la dislocation dou talon	Until it is healed.

puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then hold the patient’s thigh, and another attendant extends the limb at his hands or feet, which is placed on the collar of the limb;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the thumbs of both attendants equally, and hold the dressing either between the patient’s thighs to retain the patient when it is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the eyes equally on the dislocation at his hands, and another attendant grasps the limb at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it reaches a point, put on the plaster and stamp on it, and the strain forms, and tie the limb to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for one or two days, and if the ligature becomes loose, strain it; then unfasten it a third or a fourth time, and tell the patient to move around for three days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes forward with this, it is not certain that it will not become worse again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the afterbirth remains in the vagina, as we have already said, until it is sound.
des dois	If the afterbirth remains in the vagina, as we have already said, until it is sound.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the afterbirth is discharged, if one believes it diligently, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	If the dislocation is not at the back of the shoulder, if one believes it diligently, one must sit the patient either on the left or right side of the bed, and put the limb on what is open of these joints, then press on the limb until it returns to its place;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when they are even, and there is nothing open, if you put some salt on the root of a thistle and hold it against the shoulder for three days, then the strain will subside, and you should leave it for two days, and then remove it; and then rest it until it is healed.</p>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	And when they are even, and there is nothing open, if you put some salt on the root of a thistle and hold it against the shoulder for three days, then the strain will subside, and you should leave it for two days, and then remove it; and then rest it until it is healed.</p
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When there is both a wound and a dislocation, and it has been restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died.</p
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not confident in your skill in healing, and if you are not learned in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and punctual, do not attempt it;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	If you do not expect to bring about salvation at the outset, hold the patient’s hand and leave him to God, for if you see no hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you now reset the limb, even though the abscess persists;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is set, if you administer calming things around the burn, and cure the wound, as it should be, with desiccated ointment.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and minor bones are fractured, if the bones, do as we have said in simple ailments;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and minor bones are fractured, if the bones, do as we have said in simple ailments; and take heed not to enter into fear, as I have said, for this is worth much to you according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Explicit the pain of the flesh.
